PUBLIC COMMENT
During the public comment period, members of the public may speak on general items of interest within the Commission's
jurisdiction that are not on the agenda.  Each member of the public may speak for a maximum of three minutes with a maximum of
15 minutes for the entire public comment period. The Chair shall determine whether the matter is within the Commission's
jurisdiction. The Commission shall not act on or discuss any matters raised during the public comment period, which are not on the
agenda, but shall refer such matters to staff for review and/or request such matters be placed on a future agenda.
PUBLIC HEARING
Planning Commission decisions are final unless appealed to the City Council in accordance with Section 27.08.090 and Section
27.08.060 of the San Mateo Municipal Code. The time within which judicial review of any final decision may be sought is governed by
Code of Civil Procedure section 1094.6. If any person challenges a Planning action in court, they may be limited to raising only those
issues raised at the public hearing or in written correspondence delivered to the City of San Mateo, at or prior to, the public hearing.
Some public hearings will be automatically referred to City Council and those will be indicated below.

from the California Department of Housing and Community Development (HCD) to align with current state law,

Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to Section 21080.17 of the Public Resources Code and Section 15282(h) of the CEQA
Guidelines because it is an accessory dwelling unit ordinance that is implementing the provisions of the Government
Code related to ADUs and JADUs.

SUBJECT:
2033 La Salle Drive - Zoning Reclassification, Zoning Code Amendment, Special Use Permit (SUP), Site Plan and 
Architectural Review (SPAR), and Site Development Planning Application (SDPA) for an Early Childhood Education Center 
(PA-2025-012)
RECOMMENDATION:
Recommend that the City Council:
2)
Adopt an Ordinance to approve a Zoning Reclassification from R1-B to R1-B/Q8, and a Zoning Code Amendment to 
provide development standards for an educational facility and find it exempt from CEQA pursuant to Section 
15061(b)(3) (Common Sense Exemption); and
2)
Adopt a Resolution to approve the Planning Application (SPAR, SUP and SDPA) for the establishment and 
construction of an Early Childhood Education Center subject to the findings for approval and conditions of approval, 
and find it exempt from CEQA pursuant to Section 15303 (Small Structures Exemption).
BACKGROUND:
The Carey School is a private educational institution serving students from pre-kindergarten through fifth grade. Since 1955, 
the school has operated a K–5 campus at 1 Carey Lane, which is adjacent to the Project site at 2033 La Salle Drive.  The 
preschool program is currently located off-site at 3900 Alameda de las Pulgas within the Transfiguration Church.  The Carey 
School is seeking approval to construct an Early Childhood Education Center at the Project site to relocate its preschool 
program adjacent to its existing campus.
 
In 2019, the City Council adopted an ordinance establishing the Qualified Overlay District 8 (Q8) and amended the zoning 
map to rezone the existing Carey School campus at 1 Carey Lane from R1-B to R1-B/Q8.  The overlay was created to provide 
development standards that reflect the unique characteristics of the site and use within the residential zoning district. The 
current request seeks to extend the existing Q8 overlay and amend the zoning map to include the Project site within the 
same overlay district.
 
SITE DESCRIPTION:
The 0.6-acre Project site (26,380 square feet) consists of a single parcel currently developed with an 1,851 square foot single-
family residence and a 640 square-foot attached accessory dwelling unit, which was approved in 1986.  A private creek runs 
along the southern boundary of the site.  The property is accessed via a cul-de-sac and is directly adjacent to the main Carey 
School campus at 1 Carey Lane.  Surrounding uses include single-family residential development to the north, Junipero Serra 
High School to the east, the existing Carey School campus to the south, and multi-family apartments to the west across La 
Salle Drive.
 
The site has a General Plan land use designation of Residential Very Low and is zoned R1-B (One Family Dwellings).  A location

--- page 4 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
map showing the Project and its vicinity is included as Attachment 2.
 
PROJECT DESCRIPTION:
The applicant proposes to demolish the existing dwelling units and accessory structures and redevelop the site with a new 
Early Childhood Education Center.  The Project includes construction of a one-story, 5,908 square-foot building and 
associated site improvements.  The building would include six classrooms designed to accommodate up to 75 preschool-
aged children (ages 2–5 years) and 16 teachers.  Ancillary and support spaces would include a reception area, administrative 
office, and teacher workroom.  The Project also includes a trash enclosure, an outdoor play area located on the south side 
of the site, and a teaching garden on the north side.  Additional site improvements include installation of a new seven-foot 
tall perimeter fence, landscaping, and on-site parking with a one-way circular driveway.  An off-site parking facility located 
at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas, within 1,000 feet of the site, is also proposed for use by the Project. A cover letter from 
the applicant with additional information about the proposed use is included as Attachment 3, and the Project plans are 
included as Attachment 4.
 
APPLICABLE CODE AND POLICY REVIEW:
 
State and Local Laws
The Project involves the demolition of one owner-occupied single-family residence and one accessory dwelling unit (ADU), 
and no replacement housing is required by the Housing Crisis Act.  The Project is not considered a “housing development 
project” per State law because an educational facility will be built, not housing. At the time of application submittal, in 
February 2025, the ADU was rented to tenants with incomes above the applicable affordable income thresholds.  Thus, there 
are no “protected units,” (as defined under Government Code Section 66300.5(h)) that would need to be replaced, even 
though the Project involves the demolition of existing residential units. Also, tenant relocation payments required in the San 
Mateo Municipal Code do not apply in this case because the tenant vacated the ADU in August 2025, prior to the application 
being deemed complete.  
General Plan and Zoning Code
The General Plan land use designation for the Project site is Residential Very Low.  The proposed Project provides a 
neighborhood-serving use, childcare within a residential district, which is supported by Policy LU 3.5 and PSF 6.5.  A list of 
applicable General Plan policies and a discussion of the Project’s conformance to them is included in the Resolution in 
Attachment 1. San Mateo Municipal Code Section 27.06.040(b) requires that the Planning Commission make a written 
recommendation to the City Council for Projects which include reclassifications and zoning code amendments.
 
Zoning Reclassification and Zoning Code Amendment
The applicant is requesting a Zoning Reclassification from R1-B (One Family Dwellings) to R1-B/Q8 (One Family Dwellings 
/Qualified Overlay District 8) and an amendment to the Q8 overlay to provide development standards for the Early Childhood 
Education Center.  The City has previously applied Qualified Overlay designations to private educational facilities to address 
site-specific operational needs, including St. Matthew’s Catholic Parish and School (Q7) and Junipero Serra High School (Q6).  
These overlays established alternative floor area, parking, and development standards tailored to the educational use of 
these properties. 
 
The Qualified Overlay District 8 (Q8) was originally adopted in 2019 for the existing Carey School campus to allow an increase 
in floor area ratio (FAR) and to accommodate off-site parking within 1,000 feet of the site. The applicant is proposing to 
extend the boundaries of the Q8 Overlay to include the Project site and to amend the overlay to establish development 
standards appropriate for educational facilities located within R1 zoning districts.
The Project requires a total of 23 parking spaces to serve 75 students and 16 staff members. A total of 11 parking spaces are 
provided on-site. The Project includes a request to amend the Q8 Overlay to allow on-site, uncovered parking within the 
front setback. Pursuant to SMMC Section 27.18.110(c), required parking may not be located within the front or side yard 
setback in One Family Dwellings districts. The requested amendment to the Q8 Overlay would legally allow for parking in

--- page 5 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
the front setback.  
An off-site parking facility located at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas, within 1,000 feet of the Project site, will provide 15 
additional parking spaces.  While the base R1-B zoning requires parking to be located on the same parcel or within 200 feet 
of the site, the existing Q8 Overlay allows off-site parking within a 1,000-foot radius. Extending the Q8 Overlay to include 
the Project site will enable compliance with the off-site parking facility requirement.
Another requested amendment to the Q8 Overlay relates to the awning in the rear yard. The R1-B district allows projection 
of awnings up to eight feet in height within the rear yard setback. The Q8 Overlay is proposed to be amended to allow 
awnings up to nine feet in height to project into the rear yard setback.  Although the Q8 Overlay allows for a higher floor 
area ratio (FAR) than typically allowed in the R1-B zone, the proposed building, at 5,908 square feet, conforms to the base 
R1-B FAR requirement (0.5 for parcels up to 6,000 square feet, plus 0.2 for additional area over 6,000 square feet, not to 
exceed 6,000 square feet).  The proposed zoning code amendments are included in the Resolution (Attachment 1), and the 
proposed amendment language in track changes is included in Attachment 5.
 
Extending and amending the Q8 Overlay for the Early Childhood Education Center maintains consistency with prior Q 
overlays for private institutions.  While educational facilities are allowed in One Family Dwellings districts through a Special 
Use Permit (SUP), the proposed zoning reclassification and code amendments would facilitate implementation of General 
Plan policies, while ensuring that development standards remain compatible with the surrounding residential neighborhood 
and that regulatory oversight is maintained.  With the adoption of the proposed overlay, the Project will conform to all 
applicable zoning code standards.  A Factual Data Sheet listing the applicable zoning standards and the Project’s 
conformance to them is included as Attachment 6.
 
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR)
The Project requires Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) approval pursuant to Municipal Code Section 27.08.030 for 
the construction of a new private educational facility.  The proposed development consists of a one-story building totaling 
5,908 square feet, along with associated site improvements.  The facility would include six classrooms designed to serve up 
to 75 preschool-aged children (ages 2–5) with 16 staff members.  Ancillary spaces include a reception area, administrative 
office, and teacher workroom. 
 
Vehicular access is provided via a one-way circular driveway from La Salle Drive, and one loading berth is provided along the 
street frontage of the site. Off-site loading space is permitted through SPAR and requires approval from the Public Works 
Department for both the space location and the associated encroachment permit. The Public Works Department has 
determined that there is adequate space within the public street right-of-way along the parcel frontage to accommodate 
the loading facility. Eleven on-site parking spaces are provided at the front of the property, with the remaining 12 spaces 
proposed off-site at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas.  Landscaping and site improvements include the installation of 29 
new trees along the site perimeter, which screen the front parking area, a new seven-foot-tall perimeter fence, and a new 
trash enclosure.  Additional outdoor features include the play area and teaching garden, and a private creek that runs along 
the southern edge of the site.  The proposed Project maintains appropriate setbacks from the creek to avoid any impacts.  
The Project’s Riparian Assessment is included as Attachment 10. The play area is situated on the south side of the building, 
adjacent to the existing Carey School campus, to minimize potential noise impacts on the single-family residences to the 
north.
 
The proposed one-story stucco building is compatible in scale and architectural character with surrounding residential 
buildings and adjacent Carey School campus.  It complies with R1-B building height and plate height requirements and utilizes 
materials consistent with the character of the neighborhood.  Overall, the Project design supports orderly and harmonious 
development of the site, complies with applicable development standards and General Plan policies, and would not result 
in adverse impacts. Detailed SPAR findings are provided in the Resolution (Attachment 1).
 
Special Use Permit (SUP)
The applicant proposes to establish an Early Childhood Education Center within the One Family Dwellings (R1-B) zoning 
district. Pursuant to SMMC Section 27.18.30, private educational facilities are allowed in the R1 zoning district with approval

--- page 6 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
of a Special Use Permit (SUP).  Other private educational institutions located within the R1-B zoning district with a Q overlay 
include St. Matthew’s Catholic Parish and School (Q7) and Junipero Serra High School (Q6).  Therefore, there is precedent 
for establishing educational facilities in single-family residential districts through the SUP process.  Additionally, the 
proposed use is compatible with the adjacent Carey School campus and Serra High School. 
 
The Q8 overlay zone also requires that all uses within the overlay obtain a SUP.  The Special Use Permit includes conditions 
of approval that regulate enrollment, hours of operation, and on-site activities.  Accordingly, the operation of the proposed 
use would be regulated through conditions of approval as required by SUP.  Additionally, a SUP is required for the substantial 
removal of an existing single-family residence and off-site parking facility. Because the existing residence is proposed to be 
replaced with a private educational facility, the findings for substantial removal of a residence can be made.  A detailed 
discussion on the off-site parking facility is provided in the following section. Findings and the Conditions of Approval are 
included in Attachment 1.
 
Parking and Traffic Analysis
 
Trip Generation 
A Traffic and Parking Evaluation Memorandum for the Project was prepared by Kimley-Horn (Attachment 7).  The Carey 
School currently operates a pre-school facility at 3900 Alameda de las Pulgas, which is proposed to be relocated to the 
Project site. Based on enrollment data from the past six years provided by the applicant, at least 50% of the students at the 
existing elementary school have siblings who attend the current pre-school program.  This indicates that at least 50% of trips 
generated by the proposed Project would overlap with existing trips to the main Carey School site adjacent to the Project 
site.  While the data shows an average of 60% trips overlapping for the past 6 years, a conservative estimate based on the 
lowest observed percentage over the six most recent school years (50%) was applied to the analysis. 
 
The trip generation analysis was prepared based on the Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) average trip generation 
rates for the proposed use.  A 50% carpool trip reduction was applied, reflecting that approximately 50% of students at the 
Early Childhood Education Center who have siblings attending the existing elementary school and would carpool.  The 
proposed Project is expected to generate a net increase of 133 daily trips, including 28 net new trips during the AM peak 
hour, 27 net new trips during the school PM peak hour (3:00pm), and 27 net new trips during the PM peak hour.
 
Vehicle Miles Traveled
The project is exempt from Vehicle Miles Traveled (VMT) analysis pursuant to California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Guidelines Section 15064.3.  Under CEQA, Projects that do not exceed applicable thresholds of significance are presumed to 
have a less-than-significant VMT impact. The City has established these thresholds in its Traffic Impact Analysis Guidelines.  
According to the guidelines, local-serving retail and public service uses of 50,000 square feet or less are generally presumed 
to have a less-than-significant impact. The guidelines allow the determination of a local-serving use based on a Project’s 
location, characteristics, surrounding area, and the types of goods or services provided. Schools and educational facilities 
are recognized by the City and many other jurisdictions as local-serving uses due to their operational characteristics.  It is 
common practice to evaluate whether a proposed use generates travel patterns similar to those of retail uses identified in 
the guidelines.  This approach is consistent with the reasoning applied to retail uses, which typically redistribute existing 
trips rather than generate new ones. Similarly, educational facilities generally do not create new students; rather, students 
shift enrollment from other schools. Accordingly, the proposed educational facility while relocating operations from 3900 
Alameda de las Pulgas to the Project site is expected to redistribute existing trips rather than generate new trips.  Therefore, 
the facility qualifies as a local-serving use under 50,000 square feet and is therefore exempt from VMT analysis.
 
Local Transportation Analysis
While the Project is exempt from VMT analysis under CEQA, it is required to comply with the Local Transportation Analysis 
of the City’s Transportation Impact Analysis Guidelines.  In accordance with these guidelines, a traffic operations study was 
conducted for the nearest intersection at W. 20th Avenue and La Salle Drive.  The analysis evaluated intersection 
performance during the AM, school PM, and commute PM peak hours using collected traffic counts.
 
The traffic study evaluated Level of Service (LOS) and vehicle queuing to assess potential changes in traffic operations

--- page 7 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
resulting from the Project.  Incorporating a 50% carpool rate, the analysis concluded that the intersection would continue 
to operate at an acceptable level of LOS C or better during all peak periods.  Condition 56 has been included to ensure that 
an average trip overlap with Carey School of at least 50% is maintained throughout Project operations.
 
A queuing analysis was conducted to evaluate potential vehicle queues within the La Salle cul-de-sac and the Project 
driveway. As a conservative approach, the arrival rate assumed that all peak-hour vehicles would arrive in a linear 
distribution within the 25-minute peak period. Overall, the Project is expected to result in a queue of approximately 2.5 
vehicles within the parking lot and increase existing La Salle cul-de-sac queues by no more than one vehicle (approximately 
25 feet). Thus, the Project complies with the City’s Transportation Impact Analysis Guidelines. 
 
Parking and Circulation
The proposed Project requires 23 parking spaces pursuant to SMMC Section 27.64.160.  The Project provides 11 parking 
spaces on-site and utilizes an off-site parking facility located at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas to accommodate an 
additional 15 parking spaces.  With the off-site parking spaces, the total parking supply exceeds the requirement by three 
spaces.  Of the on-site spaces, one parking will be designated for the School Director, while all remaining staff will utilize the 
off-site parking facility at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas.  The remaining ten on-site spaces will be reserved exclusively 
for parent drop-off and pick-up activities. The off-site parking facility is located approximately 500 feet from the Project site, 
which is consistent with the Q8 Overlay provisions that allow off-site parking within 1,000 feet of the primary use.
 
A parking analysis was conducted to confirm that adequate parking capacity would remain available at 1900–2000 Alameda 
de las Pulgas after leasing 15 spaces to the Carey School.  The Carey School maintains a shared parking agreement 
(Attachment 9) with the property owner for 45 parking spaces, of which 30 spaces are allocated to the existing Carey School 
campus under its current use permit (PA-2018-069), and 15 spaces will be assigned to the proposed Project. Based on the 
City’s parking standards, the 1900 Alameda building is classified as Laboratory (R&D) use, and the 2000 Alameda building is 
classified as Office use.  The combined minimum parking requirement for the site is 713 spaces.  A total of 801 parking spaces 
is provided, exceeding the requirement by 88 spaces.  After accounting for the 45 spaces leased to the Carey School, a surplus 
of 43 spaces would remain available on-site.  Per Condition 64, the school must maintain a shared parking agreement for 
the use of off-site parking spaces at 1900–2000 Alameda de las Pulgas for the duration of its occupancy of the subject 
property.  The parking analysis is provided in Attachment 7.
 
The Project is required to release a Parking and Traffic Management Plan to provide a circulation plan for locations and times 
for drop-off and pick-up to school parents on an annual basis (Attachment 8).  This plan updates the previous operation plan 
approved under the Carey School’s existing use permit to account for overlapping trips between the main campus and the 
proposed Early Childhood Education Center. The plan identifies designated drop-off and pick-up locations for each age 
group, outlines procedures, and establishes a monitoring program to ensure safe and efficient circulation.  The school will 
provide five dedicated staff to monitor and direct traffic during drop-off and pick-up periods in accordance with the Parking 
and Traffic Management Plan.  Condition 61 requires that the school distribute an updated Parking and Traffic Plan annually 
to parents, detailing circulation routes and assigned times and location for student drop-off and pick-up.

Journal newspaper more than twenty days in advance of this Planning Commission meeting. In accordance with Government

PUBLIC COMMENTS:

--- page 8 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Public comments submitted to staff during the formal planning application review are included in Attachment 11. To date, 
five community members have submitted multiple comments raising concerns about the Project, including two letters 
addressing CEQA and traffic concerns, as well as a petition opposing the Project with more than 40 signatures. The comments 
expressed concern about the traffic, parking, noise and environmental impact of the Project. Staff has also received six 
letters in support of the Project, including a petition with over 50 signatures. Any additional public comments submitted 
after agenda publication will be posted to this item on the City’s Public Meeting Portal as “Post Packet Public Comments.”
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Zoning Reclassification and Zoning Map Amendment are exempt from California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Guidelines pursuant to Common Sense Exemption (14 CCR Section 15061(b)(3)).  The Common Sense exemption applies to 
Projects “Where it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the activity in question may have a significant 
effect on the environment, the activity is not subject to CEQA.”  The proposed reclassification to extend the Q8 overlay, 
while retaining the underlying R1-B zoning, has no potential to cause a physical change to the environment.  The amendment 
is administrative in nature and does not, by itself, authorize any physical development, demolition, or land disturbance. 
Future physical improvements or changes in use on the site would remain subject to separate discretionary approvals, 
including a SPAR and a SUP, as required under Municipal Code Section 27.60.180(h) (Qualified Overlay District 8).
 
The proposed Zoning Reclassification and Map Amendment modifies the zoning designation to apply existing overlay 
standards and do not result in any direct or reasonably foreseeable indirect physical impacts on the environment. Therefore, 
the Zoning Reclassification and Zoning Map Amendment qualify for exemption under CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).
 
The development of the Project itself is categorically exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant 
to CEQA Guidelines Section 15303, New Construction or Conversion of Small Structures (Class 3). The Project is consistent 
with the example provided under Section 15303(c), which includes “a store, motel, office, restaurant, or similar structure in 
urbanized areas.” The exemption also applies to up to four such commercial buildings not exceeding 10,000 square feet in 
floor area on sites zoned for such use, provided the Project does not involve the use of significant amounts of hazardous 
substances, that all necessary public services and facilities are available, and that the surrounding area is not environmentally 
sensitive.
 
Specifically, the proposed Project meets the criteria for this exemption as it:

Is located within an urbanized area;

Has a total floor area of less than 10,000 square feet;

Is located on a site zoned for the proposed use, as the base R1-B zoning district allows educational facilities with 
approval of a Special Use Permit (SUP);

Does not involve the use of significant amounts of hazardous substances; and

Is not located in an environmentally sensitive area, as demonstrated in the Riparian Setback Assessment 
(Attachment 10), which confirms that the on-site creek contains no riparian vegetation and does not support 
wetland habitat.
For these reasons, the proposed Project qualifies for a categorical exemption under CEQA Guidelines Section 15303.

CITY OF SAN MATEO RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2025)  
  
A RESOLUTION OF THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, RECOMMENDING 
AMENDING TITLE 27 OF THE SAN MATEO MUNICAPAL CODE RELATED TO QUALIFIED OVERLAY 8 (Q8), 
AMENDING THE ZONING MAP OF THE ZONING MAP OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO TO REZONE THE SITE 
AT 2033 LA SALLE DRIVE FROM R1-B TO R1-B/Q8, AND APPROVING THE SITE PLAN AND 
ARCHITECTURAL REVIEW (SPAR), SPECIAL USE PERMIT (SUP), AND SITE DEVELOPMENT PLANNING 
APPLICATION (SDPA) FOR DEVELOPMENT OF AN EARLY CHILDHOOD EDUCATION CENTER AT 2033 LA 
SALLE DRIVE 
 
WHEREAS, the Carey School (hereinafter referred to as the “Applicant”) submitted Planning 
Application No. PA-2025-012  on February 14, 2025 for a Zoning Reclassiﬁcation, Zoning Map Amendment, 
Site Plan and Architectural Review, Special Use Permit, and Site Development Planning Approval to rezone 
the property located at 2033 La Salle Drive from R1-B to R1-B/Q8, amend the Q8 overlay, and to establish 
and construct an early childhood education center at the same location (collectively referred to as the 
“Project”) in the City of San Mateo (“City”); and 
 
WHEREAS, the General Plan’s Public Services Facilities Element has a goal to “foster the healthy 
development and education of children of all abilities, incomes, and backgrounds,” and a speciﬁc policy 
that encourages childcare centers in residential neighborhoods where they meet the City standards (Policy 
PSF 6.5); and 
 
WHEREAS, educational facilities are permitted in the R1-B zoning district with a Special Use Permit, 
and the Q8 overlay was established to provide ﬂexible development standards to support educational 
facilities within the R1-B zoning district; and 
 
WHEREAS, in accordance with Government Code Section 65854, notice of the public hearing was 
published in the San Mateo Daily Journal, and property owners, residential tenants, and business tenants 
within one thousand (1,000) feet of the project site were notiﬁed at least twenty (20) days prior to the 
Planning Commission meeting; and 
WHEREAS, on December 9, 2025, the Planning Commission held a duly noticed public hearing, at 
which time the Commission received and considered written and oral evidence, and by a vote of 
_________ recommended that the City Council approve the Zoning Reclassiﬁcation, Zoning Map 
Amendment, Site Plan and Architectural Review, Special Use Permit, and Site Development Planning 
Application subject to the listed Findings for Approval and Conditions of Approval for Planning Application 
No. PA-2025-012.  
 
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, THAT THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN 
MATEO, CALIFORNIA HEREBY ﬁnds and determines that, based on substantial evidence in the record: 
1. The Planning Commission recommends that the City Council adopt the Ordinance (Exhibit A) to 
approve a Zoning Reclassiﬁcation from R1-B to R1-B/Q8, and a Zoning Code Amendment to 
provide development standards for an educational facility. The proposed zoning amendment to 
One Family Dwellings, Qualiﬁed District Overlay 8 is in conformance with the Residential Very Low 
land use designation of the General Plan of the City of San Mateo, because it establishes

--- page 11 ---
development standards for an educational facility that provides childcare services within a 
residential district, which is encouraged by the General Plan. 
2. The Planning Commission recommends that the City Council, pursuant to California Environmental 
Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines Common Sense exemption Section 15061(b)(3), determine the 
zoning reclassiﬁcation and the zoning map amendment is exempt from further environmental 
review because the zoning overlay does not authorize any physical development or ground 
disturbance on the Site that would result in any physical changes to the environment. 
3. The Planning Commission recommends that the City Council adopt the Resolution (Exhibit B) to 
approve the Site Plan and Architectural Review, Special Use Permit, and Site Development 
Planning Application for the establishment and construction of an early childhood education 
center in R1-B zoning district. The project includes construction of a one-story, 5,908 square-foot 
building which is compatible in scale and architectural character with surrounding residential 
buildings. Additionally, the operation is regulated through conditions of approval as required by a 
Special Use Permit.   
4. The Planning Commission recommends that the City Council, pursuant to Section 15303 (Class 3) 
of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines, determine that the proposed 
development is exempt from further environmental review because it involves the construction 
of a structure of less than 10,000 square feet within an urbanized area, does not involve the use 
of signiﬁcant amounts of hazardous substances, and is not located within an environmentally 
sensitive area.

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
DRAFT ORDINANCE NO. ____ (2025) 
AMENDING TITLE 27 OF THE SAN MATEO MUNICIPAL CODE, RELATED TO QUALIFIED OVERLAY 8 (Q8) 
DISTRICTS TO ESTABLISH DEVELOPMENT STANDARDS FOR THE PROPOSED EARLY CHILDHOOD EDUCATION 
CENTER IN THE Q8 OVERLAY AND AMENDING THE ZONING MAP OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO TO REZONE THE 
SITE AT 2033 LA SALLE DRIVE FROM R1-B (ONE FAMILY DWELLINGS) TO R1-B/Q8 (ONE FAMILY DWELLINGS, 
QUALIFIED OVERLAY DISTRICT 8) 
WHEREAS, on June 17, 2019, the City Council established the Qualified Overlay District 8 (Q8) designation 
to provide for the development of land pursuant to standards and regulations that reflect the unique 
characteristics of educational facilities within residential districts; and 
WHEREAS, the Carey School (hereinafter referred to as the “Applicant”) submitted Planning Application 
No. PA‐2025‐012 to the Planning Division for a Zoning Reclassification, Zoning Map Amendment, Site Plan and 
Architectural Review, Special Use Permit, and Site Development Planning Application to rezone the property 
located at 2033 La Salle Drive from R1-B to R1-B/Q8, and to establish and construct an early childhood education 
center at the same location (collectively referred to as the “Project”) in the City of San Mateo (“City”); and  
WHEREAS, the City has previously applied Qualified Overlay designations to private educational facilities 
to address site-specific operational needs; and  
WHEREAS, the General Plan 2040 Public Services Facilities Element has a goal to “foster the healthy 
development and education of children of all abilities, incomes, and backgrounds,” (Goal PSF-6) and a specific 
policy that encourages childcare centers in residential neighborhoods where they meet the City standards (Policy 
PSF 6.5); and  
WHEREAS, educational facilities are permitted in the R1-B zoning district with a Special Use Permit; 
however, the single-family development standards do not address the site-specific operational needs of such 
facilities; and  
WHEREAS, the Q8 Overlay addresses the unique characteristics of the educational facility, while limiting 
the uses on the site and protecting the surrounding uses by requiring a Special Use Permit for all uses within this 
overlay; and  
WHEREAS, the zoning reclassification from R1-B to R1-B/Q8 and zoning code amendment would 
implement the General Plan by establishing site specific development standards for an educational facility that 
provides childcare services while protecting the surrounding users; and  
WHEREAS, on December 9, 2025, the Planning Commission held a duly noticed public hearing, at which 
time the Commission received and considered written and oral evidence, and by a vote of ________ 
recommended that the City Council approve the Zoning Reclassification, Zoning Map Amendment, Site Plan and 
Architectural Review, Special Use Permit, and Site Development Planning Application, subject to the Findings for 
Approval and Conditions of Approval for Planning Application No. PA‐2025‐012; and

--- page 13 ---
WHEREAS, the City Council has determined that the proposed rezoning and zoning code amendments are 
consistent with the City’s General Plan because the Q8 overlay zone authorizes deviations from the standards of 
the underlying R1-B zoning district, the Project includes a Special Use Permit that limits uses on the site and 
protects the surrounding neighborhood, and the Project otherwise conforms with the Residential Very Low land 
use designation of the site.  
NOW, THEREFORE, THE COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS: 
Section 1. Subsection (h) of Section 27.60.180 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
(h) Q8 (Qualified Overlay District 8) - Limitations and Conditions. The following limitations and 
conditions shall pertain to the use of the property zoned Q8: 
(1) Uses. All uses in this district shall require a special use permit, as set forth in Chapter 27.74 of 
the Zoning Code. 
(2) Development.  Future development in this district shall comply with the site plans and 
conditions of approval in all applicable Planning Applications. Development standards include allowance 
of awning up to nine (9) feet in height within the rear yard setback. 
(3) Floor Area Ratio.  This district shall have a maximum floor area ratio of 0.39. 
(4) Parking.  Off-site parking facilities shall not be located in excess of 1,000 feet from the 
project site. Uncovered parking may be allowed within the front and side setback. 
(5)  Signage. Signage on the site shall be allowed in accordance with Title 25 of the San Mateo 
Municipal Code. 
Section 2. Environmental Determination. In accordance with California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Guidelines, the proposed zoning reclassification and the zoning map amendment are exempt from further 
environmental review pursuant to the “Common Sense” exemption (14 CCR Section 15061(b)(3)). The Common 
Sense exemption applies where it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility the activity may have a 
significant effect on the environment. The proposed zoning reclassification and zoning overlay do not authorize 
physical development or ground disturbance on the site. Rather, the amendment provides additional allowances 
for potential future use of the site as an educational facility; it does not approve a specific development proposal 
or permit construction activities. 
Pursuant to Municipal Code Section 27.60.180(h), all uses within the Q8 Overlay require approval of a Special Use 
Permit (SUP), and any development of the site requires Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR). Therefore, the 
proposed zoning reclassification and code amendment only change the site’s zoning designation and do not, in 
themselves, authorize any construction, demolition, or land disturbance that could result in physical 
environmental impacts.  
Section 3. Legislative findings. At a duly noticed public hearing on ________________, the City Council of the City 
of San Mateo reviewed and considered the associated staff report and attachments thereto, the Categorical 
Exemption, together with comments received during the public review process, and hereby finds and determines 
as follows:

--- page 14 ---
1. CONFORMANCE WITH GENERAL PLAN. The City Council finds and determines that the proposed 
zoning code amendment and zoning reclassification from One Family Dwellings (R1-B) to One Family 
Dwellings with Qualified District Overlay 8 (R1-B/Q8) are in conformance with the Residential Very 
Low land use designation of the General Plan of the City of San Mateo. The amendment establishes 
development standards for an educational facility providing childcare services within a residential 
district, consistent with General Plan Land Use Policy 3.5 and Public Services Facilities Policy 6.5, which 
encourage childcare centers in residential neighborhoods where they meet City standards. While 
educational facilities are currently permitted in the R1-B zoning district with a Special Use Permit, no 
specific development standards exist to address the unique characteristics of such uses within 
residential areas. The Qualified Overlay designations have previously been applied to private 
educational facilities to address site-specific operational needs. Extending the Q8 Overlay and 
amending the Zoning Code would implement the General Plan policies by establishing tailored 
development standards that facilitate the development of educational facilities in appropriate 
residential settings.   
2. INTENT OF ZONING CODE. The overlay district and rezoning conform to the purpose of Municipal Code 
Section 27.60.180 in that the rezoning provides standards for the use of land with unique site 
characteristics as a private educational facility.  
Section 4. Zoning Map. The Zoning Map of the City of San Mateo is hereby amended to indicate as follows:  the 
property generally known as APN: 039-040-080 as depicted in Exhibit A, attached hereto, shall be reclassified from 
the R1-B (One Family Dwellings ) Zoning District to the R1-B/Q8 (One Family Dwellings , Qualified Overlay District 
8) Zoning District and the Zoning Map shall be amended to reflect this reclassification. 
Section 5. Severability. In the event any section, clause or provision of this ordinance shall be determined invalid 
or unconstitutional, such section, clause or provision shall be deemed severable and all other sections or portions 
hereof shall remain in full force and effect. The City Council hereby declares that it would have passed this 
ordinance and each section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase thereof, irrespective of the fact that any one 
or more section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase be declared unconstitutional.  
Section 6. Publication. This Ordinance shall be published in summary in a newspaper of general circulation, 
posted in the City Clerk's Office, and posted on the City's website, all in accord with Section 2.15 of the City Charter. 
Section 7. Legislative History and Effective Date. This ordinance was introduced on Clerk to complete., and 
adopted on Clerk to complete., and shall be effective 30 days after its adoption.

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
DRAFT RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2025) 
 
APPROVING THE SITE PLAN AND ARCHITECTURAL REVIEW (SPAR), SPECIAL USE PERMIT (SUP), AND SITE 
DEVELOPMENT PLANNING APPLICATION (SDPA) FOR THE DEVELOPMENT OF AN EARLY CHILDHOOD 
EDUCATION CENTER AT 2033 LA SALLE DRIVE (PA-2018-069) 
 
WHEREAS, the Carey School (hereinafter referred to as the “Applicant”) submitted Planning Application 
No. PA‐2025‐012 to the Planning Division for a Zoning Reclassification, Zoning Map Amendment, Site Plan and 
Architectural Review, Special Use Permit, and Site Development Planning Application to rezone the property 
located at 2033 La Salle Drive from R1-B to R1-B/Q8, and to establish and construct an early childhood education 
center at the same location (collectively referred to as the “Project”) in the City of San Mateo (“City”); and 
 
WHEREAS, the San Mateo City Chapter and Municipal Code Section 27.06.050 requires final action from 
the City Council for projects which include reclassifications and which are subject to Planning Commission review 
under 27.06.040; and 
WHEREAS, on December 9, 2025, the Planning Commission held a duly noticed public hearing, at which 
time the Commission received and considered written and oral evidence, and by a vote of ________  
recommended that the City Council approve the Zoning Reclassification, Zoning Map Amendment, Site Plan and 
Architectural Review, Special Use Permit, and Site Development Planning Application, subject to the Findings for 
Approval and Conditions of Approval for Planning Application No. PA‐2025‐012. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, BY THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY 
FINDS AND RESOLVES THAT:  
In accordance with the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines, the proposed Project is 
exempt from further environmental review pursuant to Section 15303, Class 3 (New Construction or 
Conversion of Small Structures). Class 3 exemptions include the construction of small facilities or structures 
of less than 10,000 square feet, such as stores, offices, restaurants, or similar buildings in urbanized areas. 
The Project involves the construction of a single-story, approximately 5,908-square-foot building within an 
urbanized area on a site zoned R1-B, which allows educational facilities with a Special Use Permit (SUP). 
Additionally, the Project does not involve the use of hazardous substances beyond typical household cleaners. 
Therefore, the Project qualifies for the Class 3 exemption and is exempt from further environmental review 
under CEQA. 
 
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, BY THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, AS FOLLOWS: 
 
General Plan Conformance 
1. The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Land Use Element. 
 
a. Policy LU 3.5 Support Service Uses. Encourage businesses that provide a variety of services, such as 
restaurants, child care facilities, medical clinics, gyms, pharmacies, hardware stores, and grocery 
stores in locations that serve residential neighborhoods and commercial/office uses. Prioritize the 
development of these services in equity priority communities in the city. 
b. Action LU 3.19 Major Institutions/Special Facilities. Work with relevant agencies and organizations 
to support the long-term viability of major institutions and special facilities that provide important 
recreational, educational, or medical services, such as the San Mateo County Events Center, College 
of San Mateo, San Mateo County Hospital, Mills Health Center, and Peninsula Golf and Country Club.

--- page 17 ---
Require a Specific Plan and/or Master Plan to guide reuse or redevelopment of institutions and special 
facilities when appropriate. 
c. Policy LU 11.1 Economic Development. Prioritize the retention and expansion of existing businesses 
and attract new businesses that strengthen and diversify the City’s economic base. 
 
The proposed project is consistent with the above Land Use Element policies in that it supports an existing 
San Mateo institution, the Carey School, and maintains an essential community service by providing a 
childcare facility in a location that serves residential neighborhoods. While the site is not large enough to 
warrant a Master Plan or Specific Plan, the proposed Zoning Reclassification and Special Use Permit will 
establish tailored development standards, including appropriate conditions and limitations on operations, 
enrollment, and staffing levels to ensure compatibility with adjacent residential uses. Furthermore, 
approval of the project supports the City’s goal of retaining and strengthening existing businesses that 
provide essential neighborhood services. 
 
2. The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Circulation Element. 
 
a. Policy C 6.3 Local Transportation Analysis. Require site-specific transportation impact analysis 
following the City’s adopted Transportation Impact Analysis (TIA) Policy for development projects 
where there may be an adverse condition or effect on the roadway system. 
b. Policy C 6.4 Operations Analysis for Development Projects. Require new development to determine 
the need for new or modified circulation improvements, operations, or alignments where 
developments identify operational deficiencies that were not previously identified in a transportation 
impact fee study. Require development applicants to prepare an analysis to determine the need for 
modifications, such as signalization, turn restrictions, roundabouts, etc. Require applicants to fund 
identified off-site improvements if warranted, as determined by the legally appropriate 
transportation analysis, and as approved by City staff. 
c. Policy C 7.2 Shared Parking. Encourage new and existing developments, especially those in mixed-
use districts, to share parking between uses to maximize the existing parking supply, minimize the 
amount of new parking construction, and encourage “park once” behavior in commercial areas. 
d. Policy C 7.4 Bicycle Parking. Require the provision of bicycle parking as part of new private 
developments. 
 
The proposed project is consistent with the above Circulation Element policies in that a local 
transportation and operational analysis was prepared, and appropriate operational measures have been 
incorporated including traffic monitoring to ensure safe and efficient site access and circulation. The 
project also utilizes an existing underused parking facility through a shared parking arrangement, thereby 
minimizing the need for new parking construction.  In addition, the project provides both short-term and 
long-term bicycle parking consistently with the requirements of the Zoning Code. 
 
3. The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Community Design and Historic 
Resources Element. 
 
a. Policy CD 6.3 Sustainable Design. Encourage integration of sustainable design features and elements 
into the design of new buildings, including locating and orienting buildings to access solar exposure, 
preserving mature vegetation to the extent feasible, and using green building materials 
b. Policy CD 8.3 Respect Existing Scale and Rhythm. New mixed-use and commercial development 
should have context sensitive design that incorporates architectural styles and elements that relate

--- page 18 ---
to the scale and design of surrounding buildings, including by providing breaks in the building face at 
spacings common to buildings in the area and by stepping back upper floors. 
 
The proposed project is consistent with the above Community Design Element policies by incorporating 
sustainable design features through the use of electric appliances and the preservation of mature 
vegetation to the extent feasible within the development area. The project also respects the scale and 
character of the surrounding neighborhood by proposing a one-story building that is compatible in height, 
form, and materials with adjacent residential properties. 
 
4. The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Public Services and Facilities Element. 
 
a. Policy PSF 6.2 Child Care Needs. Support the provision of child-care programs and facilities to meet 
the needs of children of all abilities, incomes, and backgrounds through 2040. 
b. Policy PSF 6.3 Provision of Child Care. Encourage public and private agencies and employers to 
provide child-care services and facilities. 
c. Policy PSF 6.5 Child Care Centers in Residential and Employment Areas. Encourage childcare centers 
in residential neighborhoods where they meet City standards and at employment centers. 
 
The proposed project is consistent with the above Public Services and Facilities Element policies in that it 
provides an essential childcare service within the city, helping to meet the community’s demand. The 
facility is located within a residential neighborhood, consistent with Policy PSF 6.5, and will operate under 
the Qualified (Q) Overlay and Special Use Permit, which establish limitations on enrollment, staffing, and 
operations to ensure compatibility with the surrounding residential context. The project also supports 
Policies PSF 6.2 and PSF 6.3 by facilitating the provision of childcare services through a private operator 
that meets City standards and contributes to the overall availability of childcare within the community. 
 
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) 
1. The Site Plan and Architectural Review (Municipal Code Section 27.08.030) application and associated 
Conditions of Approval are approved based on the following findings:  
 
a. The structures, site plan, and landscaping are in scale and harmonious with the character of the 
neighborhood;  
i. 
The proposed one-story building is designed to be compatible with the architectural character of 
both the surrounding neighborhood and the adjacent school campus. The neighborhood features 
a variety of architectural styles characterized by sloped rooflines and exterior finishes such as 
stucco. The project incorporates similar design elements, including a sloped roof and stucco 
exterior, ensuring visual consistency and a cohesive transition between the school campus and 
nearby residences; and 
ii. 
The design of the one-story building complies with the maximum building heights of 24 feet to 
the plate line and 32 feet to the roof peak, and provides deep setbacks to the property lines 
reducing potential visual impacts; and  
iii. 
Parking spaces located on the front of the property will be screened with landscaping and 
proposed trees; and 
iv. 
The proposed development maintains appropriate setbacks from the creek to avoid any impacts; 
and 
v. 
The play area is situated on the south side of the building, adjacent to the existing Carey School 
campus, to minimize potential noise impacts on the single-family residences to the north; and 
vi. 
The buildings utilize high quality materials and incorporates an abundance of landscape 
throughout the project to enhance the site.

--- page 19 ---
b. The development will not be detrimental to the harmonious and orderly growth of the City;  
Upon approval the project is consistent with the City’s General Plan and consists of a previously 
approved educational facilities within residential districts;  
i. 
The project has analyzed traffic, circulation, and parking to minimize impacts to the 
neighborhood; and   
ii. 
Adequate on-street parking is available along the parcel frontage to accommodate loading facility 
without impeding use of the sidewalk or local traffic circulation; and 
iii. 
The design of the buildings acknowledges and respects the existing single-family neighborhood to 
the north, south, and west in their mass and bulk to reduce visual impacts; and 
iv. 
The project furthers the use of a private educational facility and would not result in any significant 
impacts regarding public health, safety, or welfare as conditioned; and  
v. 
The project will be constructed in compliance with all building codes, fire codes, and the City’s 
building security code.  
 
c. The development will not impair the desirability of investment or occupation in the vicinity, and 
otherwise is in the best interests of the public health, safety, or welfare in that:  
i. 
The Proposed project is designed in a manner that is sensitive and compatible with the 
surrounding neighborhood. 
ii. 
The project furthers the use of a private educational facility and would not result in any significant 
impacts regarding public health, safety, or welfare as conditioned; and  
iii. 
The project will be constructed in compliance with all building codes, fire codes, and the City’s 
building security code.  
 
d. The development meets all applicable standards as adopted by the Planning Commission and City 
Council, conforms with the General Plan, and will correct any violations of the zoning ordinance, 
building code, or other municipal codes that exist on the site.  
 
e. The development will not adversely affect matters regarding police protection, crime prevention, and 
security in that the buildings, paths of travel, and parking facilities will be required to conform to the 
City’s current Security Ordinance through Conditions of Approval.  
 
2. The Special Use Permit (Municipal Code Section 27.74.020) application to allow a private educational facility 
at 2033 La Salle Drive and associated Conditions of Approval are approved based on the following findings: 
 
a. Power to grant a special use permit shall be limited to those uses designated as "special use" 
within the districts established under SMMC Section 27.74. 
The proposed early childhood education center is considered as a private educational facility 
which is permitted by a Special Use Permit (SUP) in R1-B zoning district.  The proposed use is 
similar to other educational facilities such as the existing Carey School, St. Matthew’s Catholic 
Parish and School, and Junipero Serra High School which were previously permitted within single 
family residential districts.  
 
b. The proposed use will not adversely affect the general health, safety and/or welfare of the 
community nor will it cause injury or disturbance to adjacent property by traffic or by excessive 
noise, smoke, odor, noxious gas, dust, glare, heat, fumes, or industrial waste. 
The proposed early childhood education center use will not adversely affect the general health, 
safety and/or welfare of the community nor will it cause injury or disturbance to adjacent 
property given that the use and operations of the site are required to be in compliance with all 
applicable Building Codes, Fire Codes, and the Municipal Code.  Furthermore, the proposed use

--- page 20 ---
will not impact the local traffic system as assessed in a site-specific parking and traffic impact 
evaluation.   The Project will also be subject to conditions of approval at all times, including 
restrictions on construction hours and operational limits on enrollment and staffing to ensure 
compatibility with the adjacent residential uses. 
 
3. The Site Development Planning Application (Municipal Code Section 23.40.040) for the removal of major 
vegetation and associated Conditions of Approval are approved based on the following findings: 
 
a. The project will result in the removal of ten (10) heritage trees which will be replaced with 29 new 
trees as part of the proposed landscape plan. The removal of these trees is necessary to 
accommodate the development of the proposed project. All trees will be removed and replaced 
with appropriate landscaping to both enhance the site, screen the parking spaces, and create 
necessary buffers between surrounding properties. 
 
b. All concerns regarding tree removal on the site have been addressed as conditions of approval 
requiring conformance to the City's landscape regulations, through the provision of extensive on‐
site landscaping as shown on the project plans, and/or through the payment of a fee to the City’s 
tree planting fund.

DRAINAGE – The building permit plans show drainage designed into landscaping 
with the purpose of reducing volume or improving quality of runoff from the site 
shall be implemented, to extent feasible, subject to the approval of the Director 
of Public Works or designee or designee.  Where necessary, sidewalk drains per 
City Standard Drawing 3 1 120 shall be provided to direct the water under the 
sidewalk and through the curb.  No increase to the peak discharge shall be 
permitted downstream.  In addition, discharge shall conform to any non point 
source permit issued by the Regional Water Quality Control Board.  Drainage 
improvements made on-site shall conform to standard engineering practices and 
shall not allow any site drainage to impact adjacent properties.  All drainage 
capacity calculations shall be performed by a licensed Civil Engineer, whose 
signed engineer’s stamp shall appear on the calculations sheets and shall be 
submitted to the City for review and approval with the project civil plans 
submitted as part of the building permit for the superstructure.  The applicant

management plan.   Projects that include permanent structural controls for

(operation and maintenance) procedures for such control features shall be

submitted for review and approval prior to occupancy and specify the owner’s 
responsibility to ensure their ongoing effective operation and maintenance.

show drainage. (PUBLIC WORKS)

51 
MATERIAL HAULING – For material delivery vehicles equal to, or larger than two-
axle, six-tire single unit truck (SU) size or larger as defined by FHWA Standards, 
the applicant shall submit a truck hauling route that conforms to City of San 
Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 11.28.040 for the approval of the Director of 
Public Works or designee. The project sponsor shall require contractors to 
prohibit trucks from using “compression release engine brakes” on residential 
streets. The haul route for this project shall be approved by the Director of Public 
Works or designee. A letter from the applicant confirming the intention to use 
this hauling route shall be submitted to the Department of Public Works, and 
approved, prior to the issuance of any City permits. All material hauling activities 
including but not limited to, adherence to the approved route, hours of 
operation, staging of materials, dust control and street maintenance shall be the 
responsibility of the applicant. All storage and office trailers shall be kept off the 
public right-of-way. Tracking of dirt onto City streets and walks will not be 
allowed. Entry and exit from the site will use rock or rumble strips to prevent 
tracking. The applicant shall provide an approved method of cleaning tires and 
trimming loads on site. Any job related dirt and/or debris that impacts the public 
right of way shall be removed immediately. No wash down of dirt into storm 
drains is allowed. Use of a sweeper is permissible as long as it is a wet-vacuum 
sweeper. All material hauling activities shall be done in accordance with 
applicable City ordinances and conditions of approval. Violation of such may be 
cause for suspension of work. (PUBLIC WORKS) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
52 
PUBLIC WORKS CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITIES – The following provision to control 
traffic congestion, noise, and dust shall be followed during site excavation, 
grading and construction: 
 
(A) Construction activities related to the issuance of any Public Works permit 
shall be restricted to the weekday between 7:00 a.m. and 7:00 p.m. Please note, 
however, that no work shall be allowed to take place within the City right-of-way 
after 5:00 p.m. In addition, no work being done under the issuance of a Public 
Works encroachment permit may be performed on the weekend unless prior 
approvals have been granted by Public Works. Earth haul and materials delivery 
to and from the site, including truck arrivals and departures to and from the site, 
will be prohibited between the weekday hours of 4:00 p.m.- 5:30 p.m. Signs 
outlining these restrictions shall be posted at conspicuous locations on site. The 
signs shall be per the City Standard Drawing for posting construction hours. The 
sign shall be kept free of graffiti at all times. Contact the Public Works 
Department to obtain sample City Standard sign outlining hours of operation. 
 
The allowed hours of Public Works construction activities may be waived or

--- page 33 ---
modified through an exemption, for limited periods, if the Director of Public 
Works or designee finds that: 
 
(i) The following criteria are met: 
 
(a) Permitting extended hours of construction will decrease the total time 
needed to complete the project thus mitigating the total amount of noise 
associated with the project as a whole; or 
 
(b) Permitting extended hours of construction are required to accommodate 
design or engineering requirements, such as a large concrete pour. Such a need 
would be determined by the project's design engineer and require approval of 
the Director of Public Works or designee. 
 
(c) An emergency situation exists where the construction work is necessary to 
correct an unsafe or dangerous condition resulting in obvious and eminent peril 
to public health and safety. If such a condition exists, the City may waive any of 
the remaining requirements outlined below. 
 
(ii) The exemption will not conflict with any other condition of approval required 
by the City to mitigate significant impacts. 
 
(iii) The contractor or owner of the property will notify residential and 
commercial occupants of property adjacent to the construction site of the hours 
of construction activity which may impact the area. This notification shall be 
provided three days prior to the start of the extended construction activity. 
 
(iv) The approved hours of construction activity will be posted at the 
construction site in a place and manner that can be easily viewed by any 
interested member of the public. 
 
The Director of Public Works or designee may revoke the exemption at any time 
if the contractor or owner of the property fails to abide by the conditions of 
exemption or if it is determined that the peace, comfort and tranquility of the 
occupants of adjacent residential or commercial properties are impaired 
because of the location and nature of the construction. The waiver application 
shall be submitted to the Public Works Construction Inspector ten (10) working 
days prior to the requested date of waiver. 
 
(B) All construction vehicles shall be properly maintained and equipped with 
exhaust mufflers that meet State standards. 
 
(C) Newly disturbed soil surfaces shall be watered down regularly by a water 
trucks or by other approved method maintained on site during all grading 
operations. Construction grading activity shall be discontinued in wind 
conditions that in the opinion of the Public Works Construction Inspector cause

--- page 34 ---
excessive neighborhood dust problems. Wash down of dirt and debris into storm 
drain systems will not be allowed. 
 
(D) Construction activities shall be scheduled so that paving and foundation 
placement begin immediately upon completion of grading operation. 
 
(E) All aggregate materials transported to and from the site shall be covered in 
accordance with Section 23114 of the California Vehicle Code during transit to 
and from the site. (F) Prior to issuance of any permit, the applicant shall submit 
any applicable pedestrian or traffic detour plans, to the satisfaction of the 
Director of Public Works or designee, for any lane or sidewalk closures. The 
detour plan shall comply with Part 6, Temporary Traffic Control, of the State of 
California Manual of Uniform Traffic Control Devices (MUTCD), 2012, and 
standard construction practices. (PUBLIC WORKS) 
 
 
 
 
 
CDD Arborist (PA)

TRAFFIC ANALYSIS - The school must comply with all recommendations and 
findings of the Traffic and Parking Evaluation Memorandum prepared by the 
Kimley Horn dated November 11, 2025. 
 
 
The preschool program shall maintain a minimum 50% carpool participation rate 
(on a 3-year average) with the elementary school located at 1 Carey Lane for the 
duration of its operation. Enrollment and carpool data shall be submitted to the 
City at the start of each school year to demonstrate compliance with this 
requirement. If the 50% carpool participation rate cannot be maintained, the 
operator shall implement additional measures, such as reducing student 
enrollment, to ensure that the project does not result in traffic impacts. 
(PLANNING) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
57

Carey School, shall comply with the following circulation measures for daily 
student pick-up and drop-off: 
 
a) Monitors - During school drop-off and pick-up hours, a minimum of five school 
staff persons shall be designated for the exclusive purposes of facilitating 
circulation at a minimum of the following three locations: 
I. 
One staff at 20th Avenue and La Salle Intersection, 
II. 
Two staff at cul-de-sac, 
III. 
One staff at 2033 La Salle Drive Parking, and 
IV. 
One staff at Alameda  
 
b) Parking is not allowed at La Salle cul-de-sac pick-up/drop-off areas during peak 
hours.   
 
c) Loading Zones on Alameda - The designated “loading only” areas on Alameda 
de las Pulgas shall be honored and enforced. 
 
d) Loading and unloading students shall be per the approved Parking and Traffic 
Plan. 
 
e) Driveway signage on La Salle Drive – Temporary, professional grade and 
quality, removable (A-frame type) signage for the sole purpose of restricting 
usage of residential driveways on La Salle Drive by Ealy Childhood Education 
Center or Carey School  shall be placed twice a day, at each driveway apron along 
La Salle Drive, just prior to and throughout drop-off and pick-up hours. 
(PLANNING)

with the Police Department at all times that the use permitted by this planning 
application occupies the premises. (POLICE) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
69 
SITE LIGHTING STANDARDS – Exterior security lighting in compliance with the 
Building Security Code “Exterior Security Lighting” (San Mateo Municipal Code 
Section 23.54.060) shall be provided and maintained at all times that the use 
permitted by this planning application occupies the premises. Site lighting shall 
comply with the requirement of an average illuminance of 1 foot-candle, a 
minimum illuminance of 0.3 foot-candle, and a uniformity ratio not to exceed 
4:1 average to minimum. Light sources shall be capable of producing a “bright 
white” light with a color temperature between 3000K and 4000K and a color 
rendering index (CRI) of at least 65 unless otherwise approved.  This lighting 
standard is applicable to all parking lots, driveways, circulation areas, aisles, 
passageways, recesses, and grounds contiguous to all buildings. The lighting 
system shall be so designed as to limit light spill beyond property lines and to 
shield the light source from view from off site.  (POLICE)

the life of the project a video surveillance system subject to the following 
requirements: 
 
(A) The information shall be maintained and retrievable for a minimum of 30 
days.  The captured video material shall be accessible to investigating police 
personnel through some form of facility management during regular business 
hours.  The applicant shall provide proof of registration of the video surveillance 
camera system with the City through the City’s Neighborhood Eyes Security 
Team 
web 
form 
(https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/forms.aspx?FID=134). 
 
(B) Cameras shall be placed and maintained to view common areas of the 
property accessible to the public such as lobbies, parking lots, parking garages 
and entrances and exits to all parking garages, gates dividing different uses inside 
mixed-use parking garages, driveways, circulation areas, aisles, passageways, 
recesses, and grounds contiguous to all buildings.  This condition is not intended 
to require Applicant to install pole mount cameras on the property, cameras to 
view these areas may be installed on the building facing out. 
(C) The cameras in this system shall be megapixel or better CCTV cameras that 
shall be capable of operating in all lighting conditions anticipated at project 
completion.  Cameras viewing locations intended to allow routine vehicle

--- page 38 ---
passage onto the sites and/or garages shall additionally be capable of capturing 
the front and rear of all entering and exiting vehicles that use the sites and/or 
garages, and be of sufficient quality to identify the make and model of vehicles

71 
POST CONSTRUCTION BEST MANAGEMENT PRACTICES (BMP) – In accordance 
with the City’s Storm Water Management and Discharge Control Rules and 
Regulations, San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 7.39, and the San Mateo 
Countywide Stormwater Management Plan (SWMP) by reference, the applicant 
shall: 
 
(A) Owner/occupant shall inspect private stormwater treatment devices and GI 
features in the public right-of-way at least two (2) times per year and sweep 
parking lots immediately prior to and once during the storm season. 
 
(B) The applicant shall pay a fee on a yearly basis for cost associated with, but 
not limited to, City inspection of the private stormwater treatment facilities, 
emergency maintenance needed to protect public health or watercourses, and 
facility replacement or repair in the event that the treatment facility is no longer 
able to meet performance standards or has deteriorated. The fee shall be based 
upon the Comprehensive Fee Schedule, established by the City Council, in effect 
at the time. 
 
(C) Label new and redeveloped storm drain inlets with the phrase “No Dumping 
– Drains to Bay” plaques to alert the public to the destination of storm water and 
to prevent direct discharge of pollutants into the storm drain. Template ordering 
information is available from the Department of Public Works. 
 
(D) All process equipment, oils fuels, solvents, coolants, fertilizers, pesticides, 
and similar chemical products, as well as petroleum based wastes, tallow, and 
grease planned for storage outdoors shall be stored in covered containers at all 
times. (PUBLIC WORKS)

applies. (PUBLIC WORKS)
