CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  2
Section Name: PUBLIC HEARING
Account Number: 
File ID: 25-10657
TO:
Planning Commission
FROM:
Zachary Dahl, Director
PREPARED BY:
Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
December 9, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Accessory Dwelling Unit Ordinance – Zoning Code Amendments
RECOMMENDATION:
Recommend that the City Council introduce an Ordinance to amend the San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 27.19, 
“Accessory Dwelling Unit and Junior Accessory Dwelling Unit – Residential Zones” to address comments from the California 
Department of Housing and Community Development (HCD) to align with current state law, and to address Housing 
Element programs. 
BACKGROUND:
Since 2016, the State Legislature has passed several state laws to streamline permitting and promote construction of 
Accessory Dwelling Units (ADUs) across California. The City of San Mateo adopted its current local ADU Ordinance on 
March 21, 2022 to implement local regulations for ADUs in line with State law, and with City Council directing staff to 
provide annual updates on implementation. Since adoption in 2022, the City has seen significant ADU permitting and 
construction activity, with over 300 permits issued (164 of which have been finaled) over the past three and half years (an 
average of 87 permits issued per year).
As part of the City’s adopted Housing Element (2023-2031), the City prioritized increased ADU production (Policy H1.4) and 
supported it with six implementation actions, including an action focused on amending the City’s ADU Ordinance to align it 
with current State law and to resolve any inconsistencies identified by the California Department of Housing and 
Community Development (HCD). In October 2024, the City received a letter from HCD summarizing the agency’s review of 
the City’s ADU Ordinance (Attachment 3). HCD has had statutory authority to review local agencies’ ADU Ordinances since 
2016, and as of January 1, 2024, also has authority to enforce all State ADU laws. The HCD letter identified specific 
ordinance provisions requiring updates or clarification. An official City response letter was sent to HCD in November 2024 
(Attachment 4), with a stated goal to update the ADU Ordinance in 2025. 
In January 2025, HCD also published an updated ADU Handbook1  addressing frequently asked questions and summarizing 
recent changes to State ADU law. One notable change is Senate Bill (SB) 1211, effective January 1, 2025, which allows for 
up to eight detached ADUs to be constructed on a lot with an existing multifamily dwelling, provided that the number of 
ADUs does not exceed the number of existing units on the lot. 
On August 26, 2025, a Planning Commission study session was held to introduce ADU Ordinance updates and receive 
Commission feedback. During this study session, the Planning Commission provided staff with feedback on specific local 
changes, outside of those required for State law compliance, in order to address community needs.  Following the study 
session, staff conducted outreach and hosted a virtual workshop on local ADU regulations and proposed changes on 
September 25, 2025. The workshop included a staff presentation, polling questions to collect information and feedback, 
and time for attendees to ask questions related to the proposed ADU Ordinance update effort. Information related to this 
1 ADU Handbook link

--- page 288 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
policy effort is included on the City’s Policy and Zoning Code Update page.
DISCUSSION:
Proposed Ordinance Amendments
The proposed ADU Ordinance amendments are included in the Draft Ordinance (Attachment 1). A version with track to 
show where edits have been proposed to the existing ADU Ordinance text is also included as Attachment 2. Some of these 
edits are more minor/structural to improve organization for clarity, while other changes would result in a change to 
existing ADU development standards. A complete summary of those changes that result in a new or changed ADU 
development standard is discussed below. 
Changes Proposed in Response to HCD Comments and State Law Compliance
The changes listed below have been made primarily to address specific comments provided by HCD in their review of the 
City’s ADU Ordinance. These changes include updates to areas of the Ordinance that are either directly inconsistent with 
State ADU law, or where additional clarification was requested by HCD to demonstrate State law compliance. 
1.
ADU Definition
HCD provided a comment noting that the City’s ADU definition only includes reference to single-family ADUs. This 
is inconsistent with State law, as ADUs must be allowed on lots with single-family or multifamily dwellings. 
Therefore, a new ADU definition is proposed as follows: “Accessory dwelling unit” (ADU) means an attached or 
detached residential dwelling unit which provides complete independent living facilities for one or more persons, 
is accessory to the primary residential dwelling unit(s), and includes permanent provisions for living, sleeping, 
eating, cooking facilities and sanitation on the same lot as a Single-Family Dwelling Structure or Multifamily 
Dwelling Structure is or will be situated.”
2.
Multifamily Dwelling Structure Definition
The City’s existing Ordinance includes a definition for “Multiple Family Dwelling”, which is defined as “a building or 
portion thereof, designed or altered for occupancy by three or more families living independently of each other”. 
Additionally, the City’s existing Ordinance includes a separate definition for “Two-family dwelling”, which is 
defined as “a building(s) designed or altered to provide attached (duplex) or detached dwelling units for occupancy 
by two families living independently of each other.” HCD provided a comment to indicate that these definitions are 
inconsistent with the types of unit configurations that HCD would consider to qualify as “multifamily dwellings.” 
For the purposes of State ADU law, two or more attached units on a lot are considered multifamily, and individual 
detached units (even if there are multiple detached units on one lot) would be considered single-family. 
To address this comment, a new definition for “Multifamily Dwelling Structure” has been added that is only 
applicable to ADU development. Consistent with State ADU law, the added definition for “Multifamily Dwelling 
Structure” refers to “a structure with two or more attached primary residential dwelling units.” 
3.
Allowance for Separate Sale of ADUs per Government Code Section 66341
The City’s existing ordinance prohibits ADUs from being sold separately from the primary residence, with no 
exceptions specified. HCD identified that this is inconsistent with Government Code Section 66341, which requires 
that the City allow for separate sale of ADUs that are built or developed by a qualified nonprofit corporation, with 
additional specific qualifying criteria. Therefore, the update references this statute to allow for separate sales of 
ADUs, only when specified criteria are met.
4.
Proportionality for ADU Impact Fees
The City’s existing ordinance states that development impact fees for ADUs shall be established in an amount set 
forth by resolution of the City Council. HCD identified that additional clarity is needed to ensure that ADUs less 
than 750 square feet are not subject to impact fees, and that impact fees charged for ADUs of 750 square feet or 
more must be charged proportionately in relation to the square footage of the primary residential unit. Therefore, 
language has been added to explicitly state these requirements. For reference, proportionality refers to the size of

--- page 289 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
the ADU in relation to the size of the primary dwelling. For example, if a 1,000 square foot ADU is proposed on a 
lot with a 2,000 square foot residence, the ADU could be charged 50% of the impact fees that would be applied to 
a new primary residence on the same size. 
5.
Utility Fee Clarification
Separate from impact fees, State law allows for a jurisdiction to charge a connection fee or capacity charge for 
utilities. This charge must be proportionate to the burden of the proposed ADU, based either on square footage or 
number of drainage fixture unit values. Currently, the City’s ADU Ordinance does include a provision to require 
payment of a connection fee or capacity charge for ADUs that are separate from an existing structure. However, 
this connection fee or capacity charge may only be imposed when an ADU is constructed with a new single-family 
dwelling. Therefore, language has been added to clarify that “An ADU shall not be considered a new residential 
use for the purposes of calculating connection fees or capacity charges for utilities, including water and sewer 
service, except when the ADU is constructed with a new primary residential dwelling unit.”
6.
Removal of Reference to Variance Process
The City’s existing ADU Ordinance includes a statement that “All other zoning requirements shall be complied with 
unless an authorized variance is approved.” HCD commented that the City should amend the Ordinance to “bolster 
clarity regarding the ADU approval process,” which must provide for ministerial review under State Law. 
Therefore, this reference to the variance process has been removed from the ADU Ordinance. 
7.
Number of ADUs Permitted with Single-Family
HCD has now interpreted that State law requires that single-family lots be allowed to develop up to three types of 
ADUs, as is reflected in Government Code Section 66323. The three required types are:
a.
One Attached or Conversion ADU (from existing or proposed space within a structure) 
b.
One Detached New Construction ADU. 
c.
One JADU, located within the walls of an existing or proposed Single-Family Dwelling
HCD’s January 2025 ADU Handbook (p. 19), confirms that all three types must be allowed concurrently when a lot 
has an existing or proposed single-family dwelling, and local agencies may not restrict a property to fewer than 
these three units if each meets the applicable development standards. Current City regulations allow only two 
ADUs (one ADU and one JADU). To comply with State law and HCD’s interpretation, the update will now allow up 
to three ADUs on a single-family lot. 
8.
Front Setback Clarification
HCD commented that the City may not impose a front setback requirement that would preclude construction of an 
ADU of up to 800 square feet with four-foot side and rear setbacks. Under current local ADU regulations, all new 
construction ADUs are subject to the front setback of the underlying zoning district. Therefore, language has been 
added to clarify that “no front setback is required for a State Exempt ADU.” HCD has provided interpretation that 
because no front setback is otherwise specified in State ADU law, no front setback may be imposed on state-
exempt ADUs; however, the City may still impose a front setback on other new construction ADUs that are not 
considered state-exempt units. 
“State Exempt ADU” means an accessory dwelling unit that is created pursuant to Government Code Section 
66323. This includes conversion ADUs within an existing single-family residence or accessory structure, as well as a 
new detached ADU of not more than 800 square feet, with four-foot side and rear setbacks.  
9.
Architectural Standards – Not Applicable to State Exempt ADUs
The City’s existing ADU Ordinance includes several architectural standards for ADUs. HCD provided a comment to 
clarify that these architectural standards may not preclude development of  “State Exempt ADUs.” This has been 
addressed in the update, which includes definitions of “State Exempt ADUs” and “Nonexempt ADUs”, and clearly 
states that the architectural standards shall only apply to Nonexempt ADUs. In practice, these architectural 
standards would apply to new construction detached ADUs exceeding 800 square feet in size, new construction 
attached ADUs, and ADUs reviewed under the Accessory Dwelling Unit Discretionary Review (ADUDR) process.

--- page 290 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
10. Design Standards – Removal of Subjective Standards 
State ADU law allows for local ordinances to impose only objective standards on accessory dwelling units. 
Objective standards are defined as “standards that involve no personal or subjective judgment by a public official 
and are uniformly verifiable by reference to an external and uniform benchmark or criterion available and 
knowable by both the development applicant or proponent and the public official prior to submittal.”
In their review of the City’s existing ADU Ordinance, HCD noted that some of the design standards such as 
requiring similar exterior materials to the main home, and windows that maximize privacy, are subjective in nature 
and therefore must be either removed or amended to be objective in nature. To address this comment, the 
subjective standards referring to “architectural style of the primary dwelling unit,” “similar exterior materials and 
finishes, and family of colors as the primary unit,” “offset windows from neighbor’s windows to maximize privacy,” 
and “uniform and integrated design [when attached to an] accessory structure” have been removed.
11. JADU Interior Access Requirements
Under current local requirements, all JADUs are required to have an interior access between the JADU and the 
single-family dwelling. However, HCD has clarified that per State Law, an interior access is only required when the 
JADU does not include a separate bathroom. City staff met with HCD to discuss these requirements and identified 
that if a JADU shared utility controls (such as access to a thermostat for heating and cooling), this would also 
necessitate interior access between units to ensure that the JADU tenant has access to the shared controls. To 
address these instances where interior access is required, the update amends this language to specify that interior 
access is required between the JADU and single-family dwelling when they share restroom facilities and/or utility 
controls such as a thermostat. Otherwise, the update clarifies that “for a JADU with its own sanitation facilities and 
utility controls, interior access is not required but may be provided voluntarily.”
12. Maximum JADU Size
State law defines a Junior Accessory Dwelling Unit (JADU) as “a unit that is no more than 500 square feet in size 
and contained entirely within a single-family residence. A junior accessory dwelling unit may include separate 
sanitation facilities or may share sanitation facilities with the existing structure.” HCD commented that the City’s 
current JADU size maximum of 650 square feet exceeded the maximum unit size for a JADU allowed under State 
law. In the City’s initial response letter, staff explained that the 650 square-foot maximum size was adopted after 
prior consultation with HCD. At the time, City staff considered the more permissive maximum size would be 
acceptable if it was aligned with the overall function and use of JADUs. However, after further consultation with 
HCD following their most recent review letter, HCD confirmed that the 500 square-foot JADU size limit defined in 
State Law is what would be enforced moving forward based on a strict read of the Government Code. Since this 
direction was provided by HCD, City staff have already been enforcing this requirement consistent with State law. 
The update includes a revision to reflect this HCD guidance, reducing the JADU maximum unit size from 650 square 
feet to 500 square feet.  
13. JADU Deed Restriction Requirements
All JADUs are required by State Law to record a deed restriction with the following provisions:
a.
A prohibition on the sale of the junior accessory dwelling unit separate from the sale of the single-family 
residence, including a statement that the deed restriction may be enforced against future purchasers; and
b.
A restriction on the size and attributes of the junior accessory dwelling unit.
The City’s current ordinance includes provisions consistent with the two listed in State law (above), plus two 
additional provisions that are included in JADU deed restrictions: 
c.
The property owner must occupy either the single-family residence or the JADU; and
d.
If the JADU is rented, the unit shall not be rented for a period of less than 30 consecutive calendar days. 
As part of HCD’s review, they noted that these two additional provisions go beyond what is explicitly listed by 
State law to be included in a JADU deed restriction and they must be removed from the City’s deed restriction

--- page 291 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
requirements. Therefore, these additional provisions have been removed. However, while not explicitly listed in a 
JADU deed restriction, the JADU owner occupancy requirement and prohibition on using JADUs for short-term 
rentals are both still requirements under State Law and in the City’s ADU Ordinance. So, even though they will be 
removed from JADU deed restrictions, they will remain as requirements that must be followed.  A recent update to 
State law (Assembly Bill 1154, signed by the Governor on October 10, 2025, to become effective January 1, 2026) 
has amended owner-occupancy requirements to only apply if the JADU has shared bathroom facilities with the 
existing structure. Therefore, this requirement has been updated to clarify that owner-occupancy is not required if 
the JADU has its own bathroom. 
14. Addition of Multifamily ADU Development Standards
The current ADU Ordinance does not include specific standards for multifamily ADUs. Rather, there is a reference 
within the local Ordinance to Government Code Section 65852.2(e)(1), which previously included standards for 
multifamily ADU development. However, State Law standards for multifamily ADUs were updated under SB 1211, 
and became effective January 1, 2025. Additionally, Senate Bill 477, effective as of March 25, 2024, made changes 
to the numbering of the sections of Government Code for State ADU and JADU Laws, thereby making the cross-
reference to Government Code 65852.2 in the local ADU Ordinance incorrect (this is now under new Government 
Code Section 66323).
Most notably, SB 1211 included a change to the number of ADUs permitted on a lot with an existing multifamily 
dwelling. Previously, up to two new detached ADUs were permitted on a lot with an existing or proposed 
multifamily dwelling. However, this has been updated to allow up to eight new detached ADUs on a lot with an 
existing multifamily dwelling, provided that the number of ADUs cannot exceed the number of existing primary 
multifamily dwelling units on the lot. SB 1211 did not make any changes to State law provisions for multifamily 
conversion ADU standards, which must be allowed in combination with new detached ADUs on lots with existing 
multifamily structures. The number of conversion ADUs allowed on a multifamily lot is determined based on the 
number of existing units – at least one, and up to 25% of the existing number of units. These conversion units must 
be created from existing non-habitable space within a multifamily structure (such as attached garage or storage 
areas). There were also no changes made to State law allowances for ADUs proposed with new construction 
multifamily residential - on lot with a proposed multifamily dwelling, only up to two new detached ADUs may be 
constructed. 
To provide more clarity and reduce the need to cross reference Government Code sections to determine 
multifamily ADU standards, the ordinance update includes a new section for Multifamily ADU Development 
Standards, which outlines these provisions consistent with State law. 
Other Changes Proposed to Address Local Needs and Ordinance Functionality 
The below changes have been added, in addition to the changes specifically required by HCD, in order to address issues 
identified by City staff to improve functionality and clarity in implementing the ADU Ordinance. The Planning Commission 
Study Session on August 26, 2025 and community workshop on September 25, 2025 introduced these topic areas for 
discussion and feedback to help inform how to proceed with these updates. Based on the input received, below is a 
summary of the additional proposed changes  .
15. Addition of Definitions Section 
The ordinance update includes a new section at the beginning of the chapter with ADU-related definitions, with 
the definitions only applicable to the ADU Ordinance (Chapter 27.19). This helps to provide organizational clarity 
and will also help to clearly define the different categories of ADUs that are regulated within the Ordinance. 
16. Updates to Discretionary Review as Alternative to Ministerial Review
The City’s existing ADU Ordinance provides two paths for ADU review. The first is a ministerial building permit for 
any ADU that meets the development standards of the Ordinance (including objective standards like setbacks, 
height, and unit size, as well as some additional standards which are more subjective related to architectural style 
of the primary residence and privacy). The second option is for an Accessory Dwelling Unit Discretionary Review

--- page 292 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
(ADUDR), subject to a Planning Application approved by the Zoning Administrator prior to building permit 
application for any ADU that is not in compliance with the development standards of the ADU Ordinance.
At the August 26, 2025 Planning Commission Study Session, staff provided background on the ADUDR process and 
sought direction from the Planning Commission to streamline review by removing the ADUDR process, paired with 
more permissive objective design standards for ADU height and allowances for second-story decks and balconies. 
The Commission provided direction to keep the ADUDR process in the updated Ordinance as an alternative to 
ministerial review to provide a pathway for consideration of ADU designs that exceed the specified objective 
standards to address certain site specific design needs. The Commission was also in favor of staff’s 
recommendation to propose more permissive objective standards, expressing support for the idea that these 
changes would result in more ADU projects qualifying for the more streamlined ministerial review process – the 
proposed changes to height, setback, and second story deck standards are discussed in more detail below.  
In keeping with the Commission’s direction, the ordinance update maintains the provision for Discretionary 
Review as an Alternative to Ministerial Review. The proposed changes to this section are detailed below:
a.
Clarification of ADUDR Applicability – the ordinance update includes added language to clarify that the 
ADUDR process may be used to review any ADU that is not in full compliance with height, setback, or daylight 
plane provisions of the ADU Ordinance, but that the ADUDR process may not be used to increase the 
maximum allowable floor area. 
b.
ADUDR Requirement for Second-Story Decks and Balconies – Under current ADU Ordinance provisions, any 
second-story deck or balcony proposed with an ADU requires ADUDR. The ordinance update includes updated 
objective standards for second-story balconies (discussed further below), which would allow for small, interior 
facing second-story decks or balconies to be reviewed ministerially. Any larger second-story decks or balconies 
that do not meet these objective standards will still require ADUDR under the ordinance update.  
c.
Updated ADUDR Findings – The ordinance update includes changes to the required findings, outlined below:
i.
Removal of a finding that “the proposed ADU would not result in a negative privacy impact on an 
abutting residential lot”. This finding has been removed, as it is subjective and cannot be easily 
enforced. 
ii.
Addition of a finding that “if the proposed ADU includes a second story deck larger than 50 square 
feet, the deck or balcony shall be located and oriented to minimize direct views into neighboring 
windows or yard spaces, and screening is incorporated where necessary to minimize such views.” This 
finding has been added to provide a more objective and clear standard to address privacy concerns.
iii.
Removal of a finding that “the proposed ADU, when detached and exceeding the height limit, should 
provide at least one additional parking space.” This finding has been removed because it is in conflict 
with the proposed update to remove all parking requirements for ADUs, the language “should” is not 
strictly enforceable, and added voluntary parking provisions have been added to encourage voluntary 
parking be provided for ADUs. 
iv.
Addition of a finding that “if the proposed ADU does not comply with height, setback, or daylight plane 
standards, there are exceptional circumstances applicable to the property that would make 
compliance with the standard(s) an undue hardship, and the deviations from applicable standards are 
minimized.” This finding has been added to ensure that there is justification for the exception to a 
specific ADU development standard. 
v.
Addition of a finding that “the proposed ADU is consistent with all applicable provisions of the General 
Plan.” This finding has been added for consistency with the General Plan, and for consistency with 
other application reviews, as this is a standard finding for all Planning Applications.
d.
Updated Appeal Process for ADUDR – The appeal process for the decision of the Zoning Administrator for an 
ADUDR has been streamlined in the ordinance update to provide for appeals to the City Manager or designee, 
which could be a hearing officer.  Under the current Ordinance, the appeal would go to Planning Commission

--- page 293 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
first, then to City Council. 
17. Clarification on Max. ADU Unit Size and FAR Exemption for ADUs
The City’s current regulations do not include any specified maximum ADU size limit. Any ADU floor area exceeding 
800 square feet is regulated by the allowable floor area ratio (FAR) of the underlying zoning. Up to 800 square feet 
of ADU floor area is exempt from the total FAR calculation for a lot. ADUs cannot exceed the size of the primary 
residential unit on the property (either the single-family residence, or any individual unit within a multifamily 
building), with the exception that if the primary residence is less than 800 square feet, an 800 square-foot ADU 
would still be allowed per State law.
State Law requires that the City’s Ordinance cannot preclude ADUs of at least 800 square feet that maintain four-
foot setbacks, regardless of whether they exceed FAR. Additionally, per State law, the City cannot establish ADU 
size maximums below at least 850 square feet for one bedroom or smaller, and at least 1,000 square feet for an 
ADU with more than one bedroom.
At the August 26, 2025 Study Session, staff asked the Planning Commission to consider whether an additional 
maximum size of 1,200 square feet should be introduced for new construction ADUs (additional limit to FAR 
standards). The Planning Commission discussed this matter, with a majority of Commissioners opposed to adding 
an additional maximum size limit. The Commission directed staff to maintain the existing standards, which do not 
set a specific size maximum for ADUs. Therefore, the existing maximum unit size standards have not been 
substantially changed. Staff have proposed minor updates to clarify how FAR exemptions are applied to ADU living 
area. 
18. Height of Detached ADUs
The City’s current ADU Ordinance sets a maximum height for detached ADUs at 16 feet to top plate and 24 feet to 
roof peak. The ordinance update would increase the plate height requirement by two feet, resulting in a maximum 
height for detached ADUs of 18 feet to top plate and 24 feet to roof peak. 
The current standard is not inconsistent with State law, which requires local agencies to allow detached ADUs up 
to 16 feet in height, or up to 18 feet (plus 2 feet for matching roof pitch of existing dwelling) when near qualifying 
transit or for lots with a multi-story, multi-family dwelling, and prohibits denying a compliant two-story ADU 
regardless of local one-story zoning limits. Additionally, the HCD ADU Handbook clarifies that a local agency must 
allow for ADUs to be up to two stories, even if the primary dwelling is one story.  
The increase of plate height allowances for detached ADUs from 16 feet to 18 feet would allow for more standard 
two-story construction with at least eight-foot ceiling heights with 12-14 inches between for the floor structure. 
This height limit will accommodate a reasonably scaled two-story ADU to be approved ministerially, streamlining 
the process by increasing the plate height at which discretionary review for a two-story ADU development would 
be required. Additionally, no change is proposed to the total height to roof peak for detached ADUs, which will 
remain at 24 feet. No change is proposed to the height requirements for attached ADUs, which are currently set at 
24 feet to plate and 32 feet to peak, consistent with the maximum height requirements for single-family 
residences. 
19. Setback Exception for ADUs in Rear Third of a Lot Meeting Specific Standards
In addition to four-foot side and rear setback requirements, the proposed ordinance update includes an exception 
to allow ADUs that meet the existing requirements for an accessory structure in the rear one-third of a parcel to 
have a zero setback. 
Currently, existing zoning standards (SMMC Section 27.70.010) allow accessory structures in the rear one-third of 
a parcel to be built to a zero setback when they meet specified height and daylight plane requirements, do not 
occupy more than 50% of a required yard, and do not exceed more than one habitable floor at ground level. The 
height and daylight plane requirements for an accessory structure within required yards in R1 districts are set at

--- page 294 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
nine feet to top plate, and 16 feet to the roof peak, with a nine-foot 45-degree daylight plane. Under existing 
provisions, accessory structures are allowed to be converted to ADUs, so a homeowner could propose to build an 
accessory structure in the rear one-third of a parcel and then convert it to an ADU.
At the Planning Commission Study Session, staff recommended allowing these accessory structure standards to 
apply to new ADUs built in the rear one-third of the property rather than requiring two steps (first applying for an 
accessory structure within setbacks, then later applying to convert said accessory structure to an ADU). The 
Commission provided direction to include the accessory structure setback exception directly to new ADUs built in 
the rear one-third of a property in the updated ordinance to further streamline ADU production. 
20. Removal of ADU Parking Requirements
The City’s current ADU Ordinance requires a minimum of one standard-sized off-street parking space for each 
ADU. ADU parking can be provided either as covered or uncovered parking, and can be provided in tandem
configuration on a driveway. However, off-street parking cannot be required in any of the following instances:
a.
ADU is within ½ mile walking distance to public transit
b.
ADU is within an architecturally and historically significant historic district
c.
ADU is in part of the proposed or existing legally permitted primary residence or accessory structure
d.
ADU is in an area requiring on-street parking where permits are required but not offered to the occupant 
of the ADU
e.
ADU is located within one block of a car share location.
HCD also noted that the City must also address an additional exemption – when an ADU is proposed along with a 
permit to construct a new single-family or multifamily dwelling. 
All together, these numerous exemptions for ADU parking under State Law would apply to nearly all properties 
within the City of San Mateo that are eligible to build an ADU with just a few small clusters of sites around the 
western edges of the City still subject to ADU parking requirements.  To provide for equitable treatment of all 
properties seeking to build an ADU, the ordinance update proposes to eliminate all off-street parking 
requirements for ADUs. However, in recognition of the fact that the City still encourages and supports off-street 
parking, the ordinance includes some new provisions to encourage voluntary parking be provided for ADUs, as 
outlined below. With the existing exemptions required by State law, nearly all parcels in the City already qualify for 
a parking exemption, so this would not meaningfully change existing parking regulations for ADUs. This item was 
also discussed at the Planning Commission Study Session, where the Commission expressed support for this 
approach, with direction to evaluate additional options to support voluntary off-street parking
21. Additional Voluntary Parking Standards 
To support additional creative approaches to encourage voluntary off-street parking for ADUs and to help address 
the constraints to on-street parking in many residential areas of the City, staff have included additional provisions 
for voluntary off-street parking for ADUs and JADUs, as follows:
a.
Standard - “Voluntarily provided parking associated with ADU or JADU development must be located 
entirely on the same lot, and may be provided in a garage, carport, uncovered, or in tandem orientation”. 
i.
Rationale - Notably, allowing for tandem parking configurations here is a deviation from typical 
parking standards for single-family residential, and allows for more creative solutions to park cars 
in a more space-efficient way on a lot.
b.
Standard - “When a garage or carport is converted to an ADU or JADU, or demolished in conjunction with 
construction of an ADU, the existing driveway and curb cut are not required to be removed and may be 
maintained as parking area”. 
i.
Rationale - This is already allowed in practice, but is clarified in the Ordinance update. Typically, 
when a garage or carport is removed, the driveway must also be removed. Allowing driveways to 
remain when a garage is converted to ADU or JADU living area provides an easy and low-cost

--- page 295 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
solution for off-street parking on the driveway surface. 
c.
Standard - “A maximum of up to two voluntarily provided parking stalls may be provided for each ADU or 
JADU”. 
i.
Rationale  - This provision has been added to ensure that yard areas are not entirely paved over to 
create parking. This limit of two stalls per ADU or JADU would allow for the creation of a 
reasonable number of additional stalls, while also balancing the amount of paved area that can be 
created for parking in required yard areas, which must otherwise be improved with landscaping. It 
should also be noted that the ADU and JADU parking stalls could be provided in addition to parking 
stalls for the primary residence. There is no maximum on the number of stalls that can be provided 
for a primary residence, so long as the stalls meet other development standards (including that 
parking for the primary residence cannot be located within required yard areas).
(a) Standard - “The maximum driveway width for single-car garages may be up to 20 feet to accommodate 
additional off-street parking.”
ii.
Rationale  - Typically, single car garage driveways are limited to 17 feet in width, and 20-foot-wide 
driveways are only permitted for two-car garages or larger. By allowing wider driveways to serve 
one-car garages, in addition to the other voluntary parking incentives for ADUs and JADUs, this 
provides a larger driveway area that could be utilized to park additional cars on site. 
d.
Standard - “Uncovered parking for an ADU or JADU may be located in the required front, side, and rear 
yard setback areas. If a covered parking structure is proposed to provide voluntary parking below a 
second-story ADU, the parking structure may be located within the footprint of the proposed ADU, 
provided that it is outside of the front yard setback of the underlying zoning district. When a parking 
structure is proposed within a required side or rear setback of the underlying zoning district, the plate 
height of the parking structure shall not exceed nine feet in height”.
i.
Rationale - This provision provides an incentive to create covered parking under an ADU, solving 
for a mismatch in setback requirements for ADU living area and accessory structures. For example, 
under current requirements, an ADU may be built with a four-foot setback on a street side yard, 
whereas a garage would be subject to a 20-foot street side yard setback in R1 zoning districts. The 
above provision would allow for garage parking to be built to the same four-foot setback as the 
ADU when the parking is below the ADU living area within the same footprint. A nine-foot plate 
height limit is also proposed for garages built within required setbacks like this, consistent with the 
height limit established for accessory structures within the rear third of a parcel under SMMC 
Section 27.70.010(c). 
22. Prohibition of Rooftop Decks or Terraces above an ADU
A standard has been added in the ordinance update to specify that “rooftop decks or terraces above any portion of 
an ADU are prohibited”. This provision is added to clarify a distinction between rooftop decks and terraces, and 
small second-story decks or balconies. 
23. Allowance of Small Second-story decks or balconies with ministerial review if specific standards are met
Under the City’s current ADU Ordinance, all second story decks and balconies require ADUDR review. At the 
Planning Commission Study Session, the Commission provided staff with feedback on this process, expressing 
support for creating objective standards to allow for some second story decks and balconies to be considered 
ministerially. The Commission expressed the importance of providing standards that would ensure deck and 
balcony designs are sensitive to potential privacy impacts to adjacent neighbors. As a part of the ordinance 
update, staff have proposed that small second story decks or balconies may be considered as part of an ADU 
design for ministerial review, provided that the following standards are met:
a.
Standard – “Second story decks or balconies shall not be larger than 50 square feet in size.”
i.
Rationale – At 50 square feet or less, the deck or balcony would be small enough that it is likely to 
be used as more of a passive outdoor space by occupants of the ADU, rather than a large outdoor

--- page 296 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
area for entertaining large groups.
b.
Standard – “No portion of a second story deck or balcony shall be located within the setbacks of the 
underlying zoning, regardless of the ADU setbacks”.
i.
Rationale – This would ensure that a second-story deck or balcony would not be located closer to 
an adjacent property than would otherwise be allowed on the primary residence. This setback 
would only be applied to the deck area – other portions of the ADU structure may still be built to 
four-foot side and rear setbacks. This would provide an additional buffer between the deck area 
and adjacent properties to minimize privacy impacts. 
(b) Standard – “Decks shall only face the interior of the subject property.”
ii.
Rationale – This standard has been added to ensure that second story decks and balconies 
approved ministerially would not result in a condition where the deck or balcony provides direct 
view into the yard or structures on an adjacent property. This has been added to address concerns 
about real or perceived impacts to privacy from second story decks or balconies. 
These proposed standards would allow for small second story balconies and decks to be proposed with ADUs 
considered for ministerial review, while addressing concerns about privacy impacts to adjacent properties. This 
would also provide for additional streamlining for decks and balconies that meet these standards, reducing the 
need for ADUDR review. Second story decks or balconies that do not meet these standards could still be 
considered under the ADUDR process. 
NEXT STEPS:
Following this public hearing and a Planning Commission recommendation, the City Council will hold a public hearing to 
introduce the Ordinance, which is tentatively scheduled for January 26, 2026. Once introduced, the Ordinance would be 
then brought back for second reading and adoption at a subsequent City Council meeting. It would then become effective 
30 days afterwards. After the Ordinance is adopted by City Council, staff will send the Ordinance to HCD for review, as 
required per State law. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Zoning Code Amendments to implement the Housing Element are funded in the Community Development Department’s
annual operating budget, utilizing the Advanced Planning Fund (Fund 225), and does not impact the City’s General Fund.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The proposed ordinance is statutorily exempt from the requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
pursuant to Section 21080.17 of the Public Resources Code and Section 15282(h) of the CEQA Guidelines because it is an 
accessory dwelling unit ordinance that is implementing the provisions of the Government Code related to ADUs and 
JADUs. 
PUBLIC NOTICING AND COMMENTS:
All meeting noticing requirements were met, including the publishing of a public notice in the newspaper of general 
circulation and posting at City facilities at least 20 days in advance of the public meeting in compliance with Assembly Bill 
(AB) 2094 and Government Code Section 65854. Additionally, staff sent meeting details in the Planning Division 
eNewsletter, citywide eNewsletter, the Housing Element interested parties list and posted to the Planning Division’s 
What’s Happening in Development webpage. Prior to this public hearing, notice was also provided in the Planning Division 
eNewsletter, the citywide eNewsletter, and on City Social Media to advertise the August 26, 2025 Planning Commission 
Study Session and September 25, 2025 Virtual Outreach Webinar. 
Staff has not received any public comments on this item as of the publication of the agenda report. Public comments 
submitted after agenda publication will be posted to this item on the City’s Public Meeting Portal as “Post Packet Public 
Comments.”

DRAFT ORDINANCE 
Recommend that the City Council introduce an Ordinance to amend the San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 
27.19, “Accessory Dwelling Unit and Junior Accessory Dwelling Unit – Residential Zones” to address comments 
from the California Department of Housing and Community Development (HCD) to align with current state 
law, and to address Housing Element programs.  
WHEREAS, an existing ordinance addressing Accessory Dwelling Units and Junior Accessory Dwelling 
Units is codified as Chapter 27.19, as adopted on March 21, 2022; and 
WHEREAS, several amendments to State Accessory Dwelling Unit law have been adopted since adoption 
of Chapter 27.19; and 
WHEREAS, Policy LU 3.1 - Housing Diversity of the Land Use Element of General Plan 2040, promotes 
safe, attractive, and walkable residential neighborhoods with diverse types and sizes of homes for individuals, 
families, and households of all income levels; and 
WHEREAS, under Policy H1.4 - Support Increased Accessory Dwelling Unit Development of the Housing 
Element of General Plan 2040, the City is to amend the Accessory Dwelling Unit Ordinance to align with current 
State law and to resolve any inconsistencies identified by the California Housing and Community Development 
Department; and 
WHEREAS, on October 18, 2024, the City received a letter from the California Housing and Community 
Development Department outlining provisions in the City of San Mateo Zoning Ordinance that were inconsistent 
with State Accessory Dwelling Unit regulations; and 
WHEREAS, these changes to State Accessory Dwelling Unit law necessitate amendments to Chapter 
27.19; and 
WHEREAS, this ordinance is statutorily exempt from the requirements of the California Environmental 
Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to Section 21080.17 of the Public Resources Code and Section 15282(h) of the 
CEQA Guidelines because it is an accessory dwelling unit ordinance that is implementing the provisions of the 
Government Code related to Accessory Dwelling Units and Junior Accessory Dwelling Units. 
WHEREAS, on December 9, 2025, the Planning Commission held a duly noticed public hearing, received 
all written and oral public comments, and recommended that the City Council approve the proposed ordinance 
to amend Chapter 27.19. 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS: 
Section 1. The title of Chapter 27.19 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
ACCESSORY DWELLING UNITS AND JUNIOR ACCESSORY DWELLING UNITS 
Section 2. Article 1 of Chapter 27.19 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is deleted. 
Section 3. Section 27.19.020 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:

--- page 300 ---
27.19.020 Definitions. 
The definitions in this Section shall apply only to this Chapter. 
(a) “Accessory dwelling unit” (ADU) means an attached or detached residential dwelling unit which 
provides complete independent living facilities for one or more persons, is accessory to the primary residential 
dwelling unit(s), and includes permanent provisions for living, sleeping, eating, cooking facilities and sanitation 
on the same lot as a Single-Family Dwelling Structure or Multifamily Dwelling Structure is or will be situated. 
(1) “Attached ADU” means an accessory dwelling unit that is attached to a primary residential 
dwelling unit, or portion thereof (including an attached garage or accessory structure). 
(2) “Conversion ADU” means any accessory dwelling unit created by the conversion of any 
existing structure or portion thereof. The Conversion ADU may be created using existing structural 
components of the existing structure, or may be reconstructed to the same extent as the existing 
structure. 
(3) “Detached ADU” means an accessory dwelling unit that is separated from a primary 
residential dwelling unit. 
(4) “New Construction ADU” means any accessory dwelling unit that does not meet the 
definition and requirements of a Conversion ADU. 
(5) “Nonexempt ADU" means an accessory dwelling unit that does not meet the definition of a 
State Exempt ADU.  
(6) “State Exempt ADU” means an accessory dwelling unit that is created pursuant to 
Government Code Section 66323. 
(7) “Multifamily ADU” means an accessory dwelling unit on a lot with an existing or proposed 
Multifamily Dwelling Structure. 
(8) “Single-Family ADU” means an accessory dwelling unit on a lot with an existing or proposed 
Single-Family Dwelling Structure.  
(b) “ADU Living Area” means the interior conditioned space within an Accessory Dwelling Unit, such as 
areas used for living, sleeping, eating, cooking and sanitation, and may also include attic or basement areas 
connected to the ADU. ADU Living Area does not include non-habitable spaces such as garages, carports, 
unconditioned utility rooms, enclosed storage areas not internally accessible by the ADU, or other accessory 
structures attached to the ADU.  
(c) “Junior accessory dwelling unit” (JADU) means a unit that is no more than 500 square feet in size and 
contained entirely within an existing or proposed Single-Family Dwelling.  
(d) “Multifamily Dwelling Structure” means a structure with two or more attached primary residential 
dwelling units.

--- page 301 ---
(e) “Single-Family Dwelling Structure" means a one-family dwelling primary residential unit that either 
stands alone on a lot or is detached from other primary residential dwelling unit(s) on the same lot. 
Section 4. Section 27.19.030 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.030 Prohibition on Sale and Limitation on Rental. 
(a) An ADU shall not be sold separately from the primary residence, except as allowed by Government 
Code Section 66341. 
(b) A JADU shall not be sold separately from the primary residential dwelling unit.  
(c) If an ADU or JADU is rented, the unit shall not be rented for a period of less than 30 consecutive 
calendar days. 
Section 5. Section 27.19.040 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.040 Ministerial Permit Approval. 
A permit application for an ADU and/or a JADU is required in order to demonstrate that the unit is in 
compliance with the provisions of this Chapter. If the ADU is in full compliance with the provisions of this 
Chapter, a ministerial, non-discretionary permit will be issued.  Notwithstanding anything to the contrary in this 
Code, the issuance of a ministerial ADU or JADU permit may not be appealed. 
Section 6. Section 27.19.045 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.045 Discretionary Review as Alternative to Ministerial Approval. 
(a) As an alternative to ministerial review, an applicant may submit an application for discretionary 
review of an ADU proposal that is not in full compliance with the height, setback, or daylight plane provisions of 
this Chapter, and/or for an ADU that proposes a second story deck or balcony exceeding the standards outlined 
in this Chapter. The discretionary review application shall not be used to increase the maximum allowable floor 
area of a lot. The application for discretionary approval shall be granted if the Zoning Administrator finds all of 
the following: 
(1) The proposed ADU is consistent with all applicable objective design standards in the adopted 
R1 Single-Family Dwelling Design Guidelines. 
(2) The proposed ADU would not result in a negative impact to public health, safety, or welfare. 
(3) If the proposed ADU does not comply with height, setback, or daylight plane standards, 
there are exceptional circumstances applicable to the property that would make compliance with the 
standard(s) an undue hardship, and the deviations from applicable standards are minimized. 
(4) If the proposed ADU includes a second story deck larger than 50 square feet, the deck or 
balcony is located and oriented to minimize direct views into neighboring windows or yard spaces, and 
screening is incorporated where necessary to minimize such views.  
(5) The proposed ADU is consistent with all applicable provisions of the General Plan.

--- page 302 ---
(b) The decision of the Zoning Administrator shall not preclude the ability of an applicant to receive a 
ministerial permit for an ADU that is in full compliance with the provisions of this Chapter. 
(c) The decision of the Zoning Administrator may be appealed to the City Manager or designee, which 
may be a hearing officer. 
Section 7. Section 27.19.050 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.050 General Requirements. 
Applicability. The following shall apply to ADUs and JADUs in all zoning districts that allow for residential 
uses: 
(a) The provisions of this Chapter apply only to ADU Living Area. Accessory structures, such as garages, 
carports, non-habitable utility rooms, storage areas, or sheds, whether detached or attached to an ADU, shall be 
subject to the requirements of the underlying zoning district and other applicable provisions of the Zoning Code. 
(b) Development Impact Fees. Development impact fees for ADUs shall be established in an amount set 
forth by resolution of the City Council. No impact fees shall be charged for ADUs 750 square feet in size or 
smaller. Any impact fees charged for an ADU over 750 square feet shall be charged proportionately in relation to 
the square footage of the primary residential dwelling unit.  
(c) Utility Service. For Conversion ADUs, a separate water connection, a sewer service connection, or 
power connection is not required. If an ADU is not converted from existing space, the City may require new or 
separate utility connections. 
(d) Utility Fees. For a Conversion ADU, payment of a connection fee or capacity charge is not required. 
For an ADU that is separate from an existing structure, the City will require payment of a connection fee or 
capacity charge that is proportionate to the ADU's burden. An ADU shall not be considered a new residential use 
for the purposes of calculating connection fees or capacity charges for utilities, including water and sewer 
service, except when the ADU is constructed with a new primary residential dwelling unit. 
(e) Address Assignment.  An application for a building permit for an ADU must include application for a 
separate address assignment. 
Section 8. Section 27.19.060 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.060 Single-Family ADU Development Standards. 
(a) Applicability. This section applies to ADUs located on a lot with an existing or proposed Single-Family 
Dwelling Structure. Number of Units. A lot with an existing or proposed Single-Family Dwelling Structure may 
include any combination of the following three types of ADUs, provided that each meets the applicable 
development standards. 
(1) One Attached or Conversion ADU. 
(2) One Detached New Construction ADU.

--- page 303 ---
(3) One JADU, provided it is located within the walls of an existing or proposed Single-Family 
Dwelling Structure. 
(b) Maximum Unit Size and Floor Area Ratio (FAR). FAR and unit size maximums for both Attached and 
Detached ADUs  in excess of 800 square feet are governed by the maximum FAR established by the underlying 
zoning district and remaining floor area allowance available on the lot.  Up to 800 square feet of ADU floor area, 
including New Construction State Exempt ADUs, is exempt from the maximum FAR for each lot with a Single-
Family Dwelling Structure. This exemption does not apply to JADU floor area. In addition, the following shall 
apply: 
(1) An ADU shall not be larger, in terms of floor area, than the primary residential dwelling unit. 
However, when the primary residential dwelling unit is less than or equal to 800 square feet in size, a 
State Exempt ADU of up to 800 square feet is allowed.  
(2)  A Conversion ADU within the walls of an existing primary dwelling unit or accessory 
structure is not subject to size requirements. ADU conversions may be expanded up to 150 square feet 
beyond the existing footprint provided the expansion is used to accommodate ingress and egress to the 
ADU. 
(c) Height. The specific height maximums are applicable to all zoning districts which permit ADUs. 
(1) Attached Accessory Dwelling Units. Maximum building height for an attached ADU is 24 feet 
to top plateline and 32 feet to roof peak as measured from existing grade. 
(2) Detached Accessory Dwelling Units. Maximum building height for a detached ADU is 18 feet 
to top plateline and 24 feet to roof peak as measured from existing grade. 
(d) Setbacks. An ADU shall have setbacks as follows: 
(1) No setback shall be required for an existing garage or accessory structure that is converted 
to an ADU which is constructed in the same location and to the same dimensions, footprint, and height 
as the existing structure; or for a Detached ADU that is proposed in the rear one-third of a lot that 
otherwise meets all requirements of accessory buildings and structures in required yards of R1 districts 
pursuant to Chapter 27.70. 
(2) A minimum setback of four feet shall be required from the side and rear lot lines for all new 
ADU construction not meeting the criteria set forth in subsection (1) above, including ADUs constructed 
above an existing garage. 
(3) A minimum setback from the front lot line, as required in the lot's underlying zone district, 
shall be required for all New Construction ADUs not meeting the criteria set forth in subsection (1) 
above, including ADUs constructed above an existing garage. No setback is required for a State Exempt 
ADU. 
(e) Unit Access. An ADU must include a separate exterior entrance from the primary residential dwelling 
unit. An interior access may be provided between the two units, but is not required. 
(f) ADU and JADU Parking Standards.

--- page 304 ---
(1) General Requirements. No off-street parking shall be required for any ADU or JADU. The 
required parking for the primary residential dwelling unit(s) must comply with the underlying zoning 
district’s current standards, except when an existing garage, carport, or covered parking structure is 
converted to an ADU or JADU or demolished in conjunction with construction of an ADU. When this 
occurs, no replacement off-street parking is required for the primary residential dwelling unit. 
(2) Voluntary Parking. Off street parking for an ADU or JADU may be provided voluntarily. 
Voluntarily provided parking associated with ADU or JADU development must be located entirely on the 
same lot, and may be provided in a garage, carport, uncovered, or in tandem orientation. Additionally, 
the following provisions may be applied to create voluntary parking for an ADU or JADU. 
(A) When a garage or carport is converted to an ADU or JADU, or demolished in 
conjunction with construction of an ADU, the existing driveway and curb cut are not required to 
be removed, and may be maintained as parking area.  
(B) A maximum of up to two voluntarily provided parking stalls may be provided for 
each ADU or JADU. 
(C) The maximum driveway width for single-car garages may be up to 20 feet to 
accommodate additional off-street parking.  
(D) Uncovered parking for an ADU or JADU may be located in the required front, side, 
and rear yard setback areas. If a covered parking structure is proposed to provide voluntary 
parking below a second-story ADU, the parking structure may be located within the footprint of 
the proposed ADU, provided that it is outside of the front yard setback of the underlying zoning 
district. When a parking structure is proposed within a required side or rear setback of the 
underlying zoning district, the plate height of the parking structure shall not exceed 9 feet in 
height. 
(g) Architectural Standards. Nonexempt ADUs shall be designed to comply with the following standards, 
as applicable: 
(1) Be designed to meet the daylight plane requirements of the R-1 zoning district as applied to 
the nearest adjacent side and rear lot lines. 
(2) Provide and maintain obscured glazing on second-story windows up to five feet from the 
finished floor when the windows are located within five feet of a lot line with an abutting residential lot. 
(3) When an exterior staircase is proposed, it shall have a setback of at least five feet from the 
nearest lot line and the size of the second story landing shall be limited to the minimum area required to 
allow ingress and egress as specified by the California Building Code. 
(4) Rooftop decks or terraces above any portion of an ADU are prohibited. 
(5) When a second-story deck or balcony is proposed within a two-story ADU, the following shall 
apply: 
(A) Second story decks or balconies shall not be larger than 50 square feet in size; and

--- page 305 ---
(B) No portion of a second story deck or balcony shall be located within the setbacks of 
the underlying zoning, regardless of the ADU setbacks; and  
(C) Decks shall only face the interior of the subject property. 
Section 9. Article 2 of Chapter 27.19 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is deleted. 
Section 10. Section 27.19.070 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.070 Multifamily ADU Development Standards. 
(a)  Applicability. This section applies to all ADUs located on lots with existing or proposed Multifamily 
Dwelling Structure(s).  
(b) Number of Units Allowed. 
(1) On a lot with a proposed Multifamily Dwelling Structure, up two new Detached ADUs may be 
allowed.  
(2) On a lot with an existing Multifamily Dwelling Structure, the following ADUs may be 
permitted in combination: 
(A)  Up to eight New Construction Detached ADUs may be allowed, provided that the 
number of ADUs shall not exceed the number of existing primary residential dwelling units on 
the lot.  
(B) Conversion ADUs created by converting non-living space within an existing 
Multifamily Dwelling Structure. The number of non-living space Conversion ADUs may be at 
least one, and not more than 25 percent of the number of existing primary residential dwelling 
units.  
(c) Maximum Unit Size.  
(1) An ADU shall not have a larger floor area than the smallest primary residential dwelling unit 
on a lot. When the smallest primary residential dwelling unit is less than 800 square feet, then a State 
Exempt ADU of up to 800 square feet is allowed. 
(2) A Conversion ADU within the existing space of a Multifamily Dwelling Structure is not subject 
to size requirements.  
(3) Floor Area Ratio (FAR). Floor area size maximums for both Attached and Detached ADUs are 
governed by the floor area maximum established by the underlying zoning district and remaining floor 
area allowance available on the lot. Up to 800 square feet of ADU Living Area is exempt from total FAR 
for the lot. The exemption for ADU floor area up to 800 square feet shall be applied individually to each 
new Detached ADU proposed on a lot with an existing or proposed Multifamily Dwelling Structure.  
(4) In instances when the existing floor area allowance of a lot has been fully utilized, only New 
Construction State Exempt ADUs of up to 800 square feet are allowed.

--- page 306 ---
(d) Height - Maximum building height for a new Detached Multifamily ADU is 18 feet to top plateline 
and 24 feet to roof peak as measured from existing grade. 
(e) Setbacks.  
(1) For new Detached Multifamily ADUs, a minimum setback of four feet from side and rear 
property lines is required.  
(2) A minimum setback from the front lot line, as required in the lot's underlying zone district, 
shall be required for all new Multifamily ADUs. No front setback is required for a New Construction 
Detached State Exempt ADU. 
(f) Parking. The single-family ADU development parking standards of this Chapter shall apply to 
Multifamily ADUs. 
(g) Architectural standards. The single-family ADU development architectural standards of this Chapter 
shall apply to Nonexempt ADUs on lots with an existing or proposed Multifamily Dwelling Structure.  
(h) Separation between structures. New Detached Multifamily ADUs shall be separated from the 
primary structure by a minimum of four feet, open to the sky. Where multiple new Detached ADUs are 
proposed, the ADUs may be attached to each other, but must be detached from the primary structure.  
Section 11. Section 27.19.080 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.080 JADU Development Standards. 
(a) Applicability. The development standards in this section shall apply to all JADUs. 
(b) Permitted Zoning Districts. JADUs shall only be constructed on lots zoned to allow single-family 
residential use, or for which a Single-Family Dwelling Structure exists or is proposed to be built. The residential 
lot shall not be part of a condominium, townhouse, or other Multi-Family Dwelling Structure. 
(c) Limit to the Number of JADUs permitted. The number of JADUs is limited to one per residential lot 
with a Single-Family Residential Dwelling Structure. Lots with Multi-Family Dwelling Structures are not eligible 
for JADUs. 
(d) Setback and Other Zoning Regulations. For purposes of setbacks and other zoning regulations, the 
JADU shall be considered to be a part of the principal use of subject site and shall be subject to the same 
requirements of the underlying zoning district. 
(e) Maximum Unit Size. The floor area of a JADU shall not exceed 500 square feet, including attic and 
basement areas as defined in Section 27.04.200 for the applicable zoning district. 
(f) Construct within Existing Structure. The JADU shall be constructed within the walls of the proposed or 
legally existing Single-Family Dwelling Structure, including an attached garage. Detached accessory structures, 
including detached garages or carports, are not permitted to be converted into a JADU. 
(g) Unit Access. A JADU must include:

--- page 307 ---
(1) A separate exterior to serve the JADU only; and 
(2) When a JADU shares sanitation facilities or utility controls (such as a thermostat for heating 
and cooling), an interior entry access between the JADU and the Single-Family Dwelling Structure is 
required.  For a JADU with its own sanitation facilities and utility controls, interior access is not required, 
but may be provided voluntarily. 
(h) Efficiency Food Preparation Area. A JADU shall include an efficiency kitchen that includes the 
following components: 
(1) Cooking facility with appliances; and 
(2) Food preparation counter and storage with cabinets that are of reasonable size in relation to 
the size of the JADU. 
(i) Sanitation Facilities. A JADU may include its own separate sanitation facilities or may share sanitation 
facilities with the primary dwelling unit. 
(j) Building and Fire Requirements. 
(1) No fire wall separation or noise attenuation measures are required between the main 
dwelling and the JADU. No fire sprinklers are required for the JADU, unless the associated improvements 
meet the threshold for a "substantial remodel" as defined by Chapter 23, Building and Construction, of 
the San Mateo Municipal Code. The JADU shall have an adjoining door connected to the main living area 
for fire separation. A smoke alarm shall be required in the JADU and shall be connected to the smoke 
alarm in the main residence. 
(2) The JADU shall be equipped with a carbon monoxide detector. 
(k) Utility Service. Separate water connection, a separate sewer service connection, and power 
connection as water, sewer, and power service are not required for a JADU. 
(l) Parking. No additional off-street parking is required for a JADU. 
(m) Address Assignment. An application for a building permit for a JADU must include application for a 
separate address assignment. 
(n) Owner Occupancy. If the JADU has shared sanitation facilities with the existing structure, owner-
occupancy shall be required. The owner may reside in either the remaining portion of the structure or the newly 
created JADU. Owner-occupancy shall not be required if the JADU has its own sanitation facilities, or if the 
owner is another governmental agency, land trust, or housing organization. 
Section 12. Section 27.19.090 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows: 
27.19.090 JADU Deed Restriction. 
(a) Prior to building permit issuance for a JADU, a deed restriction shall be recorded to indicate the 
following:

--- page 308 ---
(1) Sale of the JADU separately from the single-family residence is prohibited. 
(2) The approved size and attributes of the JADU. 
(b) A copy of this deed restriction must be given to each prospective occupant. 
Section 13. Section 27.19.100 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is deleted. 
Section 14. Section 27.19.110 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is deleted. 
Section 15. Section 27.19.120 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is deleted. 
Section 16. Environmental Determination. In accordance with Public Resources Code Section 27080.7 and 
California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines, section 15282(h), this action is statutorily exempt from 
the requirements of CEQA because it is an accessory dwelling unit ordinance that is implementing provisions of 
the Government Code related to ADUs and JAUDs. 
Section 17. Severability. In the event any section, clause or provision of this ordinance shall be determined 
invalid or unconstitutional, such section, clause or provision shall be deemed severable and all other sections or 
portions hereof shall remain in full force and effect. 
Section 18. Publication. This Ordinance shall be published in summary in a newspaper of general circulation, 
posted in the City Clerk's Office, and posted on the City's website, all in accord with Section 2.15 of the City 
Charter. 
Section 19. Legislative History and Effective Date. This ordinance was introduced on Clerk to complete., and 
adopted on Clerk to complete., and shall be effective 30 days after its adoption.
